1 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martinez


No. 82,217


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


268 Kan. 21; 988 P.2d 735; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 486



September 24, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended December 28, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Ford district court; VAN HAMPTON, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State appealed from the dismissal by the Ford District Court (Kansas) of a felony count of driving under the influence (DUI), after holding that the felony provision of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 8-1567(f) (1998 Supp.) for a third DUI conviction was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with driving under the influence (DUI) in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 8-1567(f) (1998 Supp.), a nonperson felony for a third time DUI conviction. The trial court dismissed the felony DUI count, holding that, as third offense DUI was a strict liability offense, not requiring the State to prove criminal intent, the statute violated appellee's right to due process of law. The State appealed. The court reversed, holding that the trial court's reliance on precedent discussing guilt without criminal intent for a misdemeanor did not provide a basis for determining if a conviction for felony DUI is constitutional or unconstitutional; that the legislature may provide for strict liability crimes; and that the state's DUI law providing for third time offender felony treatment is one of the recognized exceptions where the legislature has specifically stated that an offense does not require intent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings, holding that the district court erred in determining that imposing a felony penalty for a third conviction for DUI was unconstitutional.

 

2 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rucker


Nos. 80,106, 80,753


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


267 Kan. 816; 987 P.2d 1080; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 410



July 16, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court; REBECCA L. PILSHAW, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a Sedgwick District Court (Kansas) decision, after a jury trial, convicting him of aggravated indecent liberties with a child in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3504(a)(2)(A) and stalking in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3438(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant, after a jury trial, challenged his convictions of aggravated indecent liberties with a child in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3504(a)(2)(A) and stalking in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3438(a). The appellate court affirmed the trial court decision. The trial court's denial of appellant's psychological evaluation of the alleged victim request was within the court's discretion because there was significant testimony corroborating the alleged victim's allegations and there was nothing to indicate that the alleged victim had a disease or defect discoverable in a psychological evaluation. The evidence that appellant allegedly abused another child in a similar manner was properly admitted under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-455 because the disputed evidence of the prior crimes was relevant in the instant case and its probative value outweighed potential prejudice. Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3438 was not unconstitutionally vague because the statute terms were words of common understanding whose meaning was not vague. There was sufficient evidence to convict appellant of violating § 21-3438 because there was evidence that appellant's pattern of conduct constituted a credible threat.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed appellant's aggravated indecent liberties with a child and stalking convictions. The trial court acted within its discretion in refusing to order a psychological examination of the alleged victim and in admitting evidence of prior similar child abuse acts under the statute. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague and there was sufficient evidence that appellant had violated it.

 

3 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Graff v. TWA


No. 82,148


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


267 Kan. 854; 983 P.2d 258; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 412



July 16, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Workers Compensation Board.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the Workers Compensation Board (Kansas) overturning an administrative law judge's award and denying her benefits under the Kansas Workers Compensation Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-505. Appellant, a flight attendant, claimed she suffered from carpal tunnel syndrome as a result of work activities performed in the airspace over Kansas, among other places.


OVERVIEW: A decision overturning an administrative law judge's award and denying workers' compensation benefits to appellant under the Kansas Workers Compensation Act (the Act), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-505, was reversed. The award of benefits was reinstated, subject to the workers' compensation board's determination on remand regarding what, if any, offset that appellee employer was entitled to due to appellant's retirement benefits. Appellant, a flight attendant, claimed she suffered from carpal tunnel syndrome as a result of her work in the airspace over Kansas, among other places. The appellate court held that appellant sustained an injury in Kansas and was entitled to benefits. According to the court, where a repetitive trauma injury was caused or aggravated by work activities, some of which occurred in Kansas, the injury was compensable. The appellate court held that the Act did not preclude coverage for flight attendants where there was no clear statement from the legislature or proof of pre-emptive federal legislation. Retirement did not preclude appellant from receiving benefits, and medical evidence was not necessary to establish the existence, nature, and extent of the injury.


OUTCOME: The reversal of an administrative law judge's award and the denial of workers' compensation benefits was overturned, and the award was reinstated subject to the workers' compensation board's determination regarding what, if any, offset that appellee employer was entitled to due to appellant's retirement. Appellant flight attendant was injured in Kansas and was entitled to benefits, and the statute did not preclude coverage for flight attendants.

 

4 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wilson


No. 80,657, 80,658


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


267 Kan. 550; 987 P.2d 1060; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 385



July 9, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wyandotte district court; THOMAS L. BOEDING, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a Wyandotte District Court (Kansas) decision convicting them of endangering a child in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3608.


OVERVIEW: Appellants challenged their child endangerment convictions, in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3608, surrounding the third-party abuse and neglect of a child living in their household. The appellant court partially affirmed and partially reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded. Section 21-3608(a) was not unconstitutionally vague, overbroad, or beyond the state's police power. The type of prohibited conduct was clear and no lawful conduct or activities were prohibited. There was insufficient evidence to convict appellant husband of violating § 21-3608; his failure to act was not in itself criminal because he lacked the requisite authority and control over the child and alleged abuser to permit the child's placement in an abusive situation. However, appellant wife's conviction was affirmed as she caused a situation where the abuse could continue by falsely asserting to authorities that the child was not in the house. Such conduct constituted taking an active role in hiding the abuse and effectively turning away help.


OUTCOME: The appellate court partially affirmed and partially reversed a trial court decision convicting appellants of child endangerment in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3608 and remanded. Appellant husband's conviction was reversed as there was no evidence that he had the required authority or control over the child or alleged abuser. Appellant wife's conviction was affirmed as she created and sustained abuse by hiding it and turning away help.

 

5 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Treaster v. Dillon Cos.,Inc.


No. 80,830


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


267 Kan. 610; 987 P.2d 325; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 405



July 9, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 2, 1999. Second Correction August 16, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Workers Compensation Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a Workers Compensation Board (Kansas) decision that determined the last day appellant performed her job duties was the date of the qualifying accident or occurrence and that appellee employer was entitled, pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-501(h), to offset the workers compensation award by retirement benefits appellant was receiving from a plan totally funded by appellee employer's contributions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee challenged an administrative agency decision that held the last date appellant performed her job duties and not the earlier date appellant sought further medical attention for the complained of injuries was the date of the qualifying injuries for workers' compensation benefit entitlement purposes. The agency also held that appellee employer, pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-501(h), was entitled to offset the workers compensation award from retirement benefits appellant received from a plan totally funded by appellee employer's contributions. The appellate court affirmed the agency decision. The date fixed for injury purposes was the last day appellant worked. Based on medical testimony, the agency properly determined that the work activity causing appellant's complained of injury continued until the last day of her work with appellee employer as it was the date in which appellant was forced to discontinue work she performed for appellee employer because to the pain she was suffering. Section 44-501(h) allowing offset was constitutional and did not violate the Equal Protection Clause as prevention of wage loss duplication awards was a legitimate state goal.


OUTCOME: Appellate court affirmed an administrative agency decision that held the last day appellant performed her job duties with appellee employer and not the earlier date where appellant was forced to seek treatment for her injuries was the qualifying date for workers compensation benefit entitlement. Further, appellee employer was entitle to offset the workers compensation award from retirement benefits it paid in order to avoid benefit duplication.

 

6 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Bishop v. City of Winona


No. 81,117


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


267 Kan. 653; 983 P.2d 861; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 408



July 9, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Logan district court, GLENN D. SCHIFFNER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a judgment of the Logan District Court (Kansas) that affirmed a Board of Tax Appeals decision sustaining an ad valorem tax increase.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city issued general obligation bonds for the construction of a natural gas system and raised property taxes by increasing a mill levy imposed on property owners in the city. Appellant taxpayer filed a tax protest with the Board of Tax Appeals (BOTA) under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-2005 challenging her real estate taxes. BOTA upheld the tax increase, and the taxpayer appealed. Appellant contended the city's bonds were payable only from revenue derived from users of the gas system and not from the imposition of a mill levy on property owners. The court rejected appellant's argument and affirmed the district court's summary judgment in favor of the city. Review was confined to the eight factors set out in Kan. Stat. Ann. § 74-621(c). The district court properly concluded that the bonds were valid and the tax was legal.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirming the validity of an order sustaining an ad valorem tax increase was affirmed because the lower court's decision was well reasoned as to the validity of the bonds and the taxpayer's argument was without merit.

 

7 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Regency Park, L.P. v. City of Topeka


Nos. 80,805, 80,806


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


267 Kan. 465; 981 P.2d 256; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 321



June 4, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court; FRED S. JACKSON, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ratepayers appealed from the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which held that they were not entitled to a refund of stormwater utility charges assessed and collected by defendant city after the ordinance enacting the charges was declared invalid in another case.


OVERVIEW: In a prior case, the court had declared a city ordinance assessing stormwater and sewer charges to be invalid because it was not properly enacted in accordance with state law. In this case, two plaintiff ratepayers sought a refund of charges they had paid. The trial court denied the claim based on the volunteer rule, holding that because plaintiffs had paid the fees without protest they were volunteers and were not entitled to a refund. Plaintiffs appealed and the court affirmed the result, but relied on an additional ground while also affirming the trial court's application of the volunteer rule. The prior court decision found that the city ordinance was invalid, but not that it was void. Therefore, the ordinance was binding until it was declared invalid so plaintiffs were not entitled to a refund for prior payments made. The court further found that plaintiffs' payments were voluntary because they did not protest the ordinance. Plaintiffs were not required to have used an administrative process for objecting to the calculation of the assessment, but something more than vague complaints to city officials was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for defendant city that plaintiffs were not entitled to a refund of charges paid under an invalid ordinance, because the ordinance in issue was only voidable and was in full force and effect until declared to be invalid. Furthermore, the court found that plaintiffs' payments of the charges were voluntary and not subject to refund because plaintiffs did not protest payment.

 

8 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Battrick v. State


No. 80,337


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


267 Kan. 389; 985 P.2d 707; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 319



May 28, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Norton district court; CHARLES E. WORDEN, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review of the decision of the Norton District Court (Kansas), which dismissed three consolidated appeals challenging the constitutionality of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-1501(b). The court found that the pro se habeas petitions were not filed within the 30-day period under § 60-1501(b). The petitioners claimed that the 30-day limitation was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In these three consolidated habeas corpus petitions, petitioners challenged the constitutionality of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-1501 which set a 30 day statute of limitation on the filing of habeas petitions. All three petitions were filed more than 30 days from the date of final administrative action on two disciplinary convictions and one parole denial. On review the court affirmed the lower court, holding the statute was not a bill of attainder because it did not contain the elements of (1) specificity in identification of individuals affected; (2) punishment; and (3) lack of a judicial trial. The court found that the petitioners here were well aware of their claims. These inmates had ample opportunity to be heard through extensive administrative procedures and a review by the district court if timely requested. The court also ruled that the statute was constitutional on its face and that petitioners could not establish that no set of circumstances existed under which the statute would be valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court which dismissed petitioners' habeas corpus petitions on grounds the petitions were filed more than 30 days from the date of final administrative action. The court held the statute applied to the petitioners and was constitutional on its face. The court found that the statute was not a bill of attainder, and did not bar the right to a writ of habeas corpus.

Miller v. Sloan, Listrom, Eisenbarth, Sloan & Glassman


No. 80,116


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


267 Kan. 245; 978 P.2d 922; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 251



April 23, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised: May 4, 1999; As Revised: May 18, 1999; As Revised: July 23, 1999; As Revised: July 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Shawnee district court; TERRY L. BULLOCK and FRED S. JACKSON, judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas) that granted appellees' motions for dismissal and for summary judgment. Appellant brought the action against his malpractice insurer, the healthcare stabilization fund, and his attorneys, claiming that appellees had in bad faith settled a malpractice claim against him without informing him or obtaining his consent to the settlement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant dentist, who was alleged to have committed medical malpractice, filed an action against appellee malpractice insurer, appellee health care stabilization fund, and appellee attorneys. Appellant claimed that appellees had in bad faith settled the malpractice claim against him without informing him or obtaining his consent to the settlement. The lower court granted each appellees' motions for dismissal and for summary judgment. The supreme court affirmed the lower court's decision. The court found that appellee fund, not appellee insurer, employed the attorneys to represent appellant prior to the settlement hearing. Appellee insurer did not breach its duties of loyalty and allegiance by not notifying appellant of the settlement hearing or retaining attorneys on his behalf who failed to provide him with notice of the settlement hearing. The lower court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee insurer was not in error. The court went on to find that appellant's negligence and fraud claims against appellee fund could not succeed because appellee fund had no duty under the Kansas Tort Claims Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. §75-6101 et seq., to appellant.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the lower court's decision that granted appellees' motions for dismissal and summary judgment. For dismissal, the court found that there was a lack of identifiable damages in appellant's claims for outrageous conduct, fraud, and negligence and the court found that there was no breach of duty of loyalty and allegiance by not notifying appellant of the settlement hearing.

 

10 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Sammons v. Simmons


No. 80,521


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


267 Kan. 155; 976 P.2d 505; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 228



April 16, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Butler district court; ROBERT C. HELSEL, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a decision from the Butler District Court (Kansas), which denied his petition for habeas corpus relief alleging that discipline imposed on him was a violation of his due process rights.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was an inmate who was disciplined because he gave a picture to his cellmate that contained symbols of a white supremacy group. Petitioner received a 14-day restriction, a fine, and lost good-time credits. Pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-1501, petitioner challenged the discipline, alleging that his due process rights were violated. The court denied the petition, finding that the discipline imposed was not a significant and atypical hardship on petitioner. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment because there was no violation of petitioner's due process rights. The symbols on the picture represented prohibited prison groups and petitioner offered no evidence that appellees' actions were wrong. Petitioner was not subject to double jeopardy because disciplinary actions under penal institution guidelines did not constitute prosecution of criminal charges. The regulations did not increase the penalty for petitioner's crime, and thus did not implicate the Ex Post Facto Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying petitioner inmate relief because petitioner's due process rights were not violated when appellee prison officials disciplined him for giving away a picture containing symbols of a prohibited prison group. The discipline was not an atypical hardship on petitioner, and he was not subject to double jeopardy where application of penal guidelines did not constitute criminal prosecution.

 

11 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Snelling


No. 80,308


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


266 Kan. 986; 975 P.2d 259; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 114



March 5, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Ellsworth district court; HANNELORE KITTS, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Ellsworth District Court (Kansas), which determined that applying the public access provisions of the Kansas Offender Registration Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-4901 et seq., to appellee, a 17-year old convicted of indecent solicitation of a 15-year old, constituted unconstitutional cruel and unusual punishment under the authority of State v. Scott, 24 Kan.App.2d 480, 947 P.2d 466 (1997).


OVERVIEW: Appellee, a 17-year old, was convicted of indecent solicitation of a 15-year old. The trial court determined that applying the public access provisions of the Kansas Offender Registration Act (Act), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-4901 et seq., to appellee constituted unconstitutional cruel and unusual punishment under the authority of State v. Scott, 24 Kan.App.2d 480, 947 P.2d 466 (1997). Appellant, the state of Kansas, appealed and the appellate court reversed. The court found that appellee was convicted of a sexually violent crime. The court further found that appellee was specifically informed before he entered his guilty pleas that he would be subject to the provision of the Act. The court held that the Act was constitutional and that it did not allow any different determination to justify the finding and order made by the trial court. The court rejected appellee's suggestion that trial courts had discretion as to whether to apply the public access provisions of the Act, depending of the facts of each individual case. Therefore, the court reversed the trial court's ruling that appellee's registration was not to be open to inspection by the public.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed a trial court's decision, that application of the public access provisions of the Kansas Offender Registration Act (Act) to appellee, a 17-year old convicted of indecent solicitation of a 15-year old, constituted unconstitutional cruel and unusual punishment. The court held that the Act was constitutional and that it did not allow any different determination to justify the finding and order made by the trial court.

 

12 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


In re Appeal of University of Kansas Sch. of Med.-Wichita Med. Practice Ass'n.


No. 79,672


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


266 Kan. 737; 973 P.2d 176; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 20



February 5, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 2, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court, JAMES P. BUCHELE, judge.



DISPOSITION: The district court's decision affirming BOTA reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant not-for-profit corporation challenged the order of the Shawnee District Court affirming the decision of the Board of Tax Appeals denying appellant a claimed property tax exemption under the provisions of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-201 because appellant owned the property at issue, but was not operating the property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant not-for-profit corporation owned property for which it claimed a tax exemption under of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-201. The Board of Tax Appeals (BOTA) denied the exemption because it found property was not used exclusively for humanitarian purposes. The district court affirmed the denial of the exemption because appellant owned, but was not operating the property. Appellant challenged the decision. The appeals court reversed because the property for which exemption was claimed was owned and leased by appellant, which was a corporation fulfilling all requirements of § 79-201, and the corporation leasing the property also fulfilled the statutory requirements of § 79-201. And, the court found a tax exemption should be granted when one not-for-profit corporation leased property to another not-for-profit corporation, and profit was not a dominant motive in the leasing arrangement, any surplus revenue generated by lease was substantially and predominantly related to the purpose of providing humanitarian services, and the property claimed as exempt was actually and regularly used by a community service organization for the predominant purpose of providing humanitarian services.


OUTCOME: The appeals court reversed the denial of the tax exemption because a tax exemption should have been granted because appellant not-for-profit corporation leased its property to another not-for-profit corporation, and the lease was not primarily created for profit, surplus revenue generated by lease was predominantly related to provision of humanitarian services, and property was used for predominant purpose of providing humanitarian services.

 

13 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crow


No. 79,287


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


266 Kan. 690; 974 P.2d 100; 1999 Kan. LEXIS 417



January 29, 1999, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Ellsworth district court; HANNELORE KITTS, judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution challenged the judgment of the Ellsworth District Court (Kansas), holding that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3437 (1996) unconstitutionally deprived a criminal defendant of the right to confront witnesses guaranteed by the U.S. Const. amend. VI.


OVERVIEW: Appellee challenged the prosecution's intent to proffer a forensic lab report into evidence to show that the substance in his possession was marijuana. Instead of objecting to the motion on the ground the conclusions of the report would be contested at trial, appellee asserted that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3437 (1996) violated his rights under Kan. Const. B. of R. § 10 and U.S. Const. amend. VI to meet and confront the witnesses against him. The trial court ruled that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3437 (1996) violated appellee's U.S. Const. amend. VI right to confront witnesses. On appeal, the court reversed. Reviewing the language of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3437 (1996) and caselaw from other jurisdictions, the court ruled that because the statute provided for the accused to determine whether the contents of a report concerning forensic examinations will be contested at trial, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3437 (1996) was constitutional under the U.S. Const. amend. VI. The court noted that it was not unconstitutional to require this right to be affirmatively exercised and that the grounds of the objection have an indicia of merit. Thus, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3437 (1996) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that the statute violated the Sixth Amendment, holding that the statute was constitutional so long as the accused had the right to determine whether the contents of a report concerning forensic examinations will be contested at trial.

 

14 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Reynolds


Nos. 79,619, 79,953


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


266 Kan. 449; 970 P.2d 537; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 828



December 18, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Johnson district court; SAMUEL K. BRUNER, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, successor in interest, sought review from Johnson County District Court (Kansas), which refused to enforce a New York court's judgment against decedent's estate and held that such judgment was not enforceable against the assets of the estate. The court allowed an interim executor and attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: In consolidated action, the trial court refused to enforce New York court's judgment against decedent's estate and allowed an interim executor and attorney fees. Appellant, successor in interest, sought review. Pursuant to Full Faith and Credit Clause of U.S. Const. art. IV, § 1, a judgment was entitled to full faith and credit when the second court's inquiry disclosed that all questions had been fully and fairly litigated and finally decided. However, pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 59-2239, a party seeking to remove something from a decedent's estate must have complied with the nonclaim statute in the absence of an express statutory exception. The court held that the trial court did not err in holding that the Full Faith and Credit Clause did not require the executor to pay the judgment out of the assets of the estate. The court held that appellant's claim was not time barred because appellant was not given statutorily required notice. The court held that there was substantial evidence to support the trial court's allowance of attorney fees and appointment of an interim executor. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part judgments of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part judgments of trial court, which refused to enforce New York court's judgment against decedent's estate and allowed interim executor and attorney fees. The court held that, although the Full Faith and Credit Clause did not require the executor to pay appellant, successor in interest, the judgment out of estate assets, appellant's claim was not time barred because it was not given required notice.

 

15 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Kaul v. Kansas Dep't of Revenue


No. 79,647


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


266 Kan. 464; 970 P.2d 60; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 826



December 18, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 15, 1999. Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 4938.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jackson district court; GARY L. NAFZIGER, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retailers sought review from the Jackson District Court (Kansas), which held that appellants were not exempt from payment of the state motor fuel tax collected by appellee State of Kansas Department of Revenue. Appellants contended that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-3408 exempted them from the payment of such tax because their Indian reservation was a "territory" or other "state."


OVERVIEW: Appellant retailers initiated action against appellee State of Kansas Department of Revenue and contended that appellants were exempted from the payment of state motor fuel tax, pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-3408, because appellant's Indian reservation was a "territory" or other "state" exempt from such tax. The trial court held that appellants were not exempt, and appellants sought review. Although appellants were Indians, they were not members of the tribe and their businesses were not situated on a reservation but on a state highway within Kansas. The court held that Indian reservations were separate and distinct nations that were protected by treaty with the United States and that the exemption statute must have been construed with such conception. However, the court held that appellants were not exempt from the tax because Indian reservations within the boundaries of the state were not included as territories outside the boundaries of the state, a statutory requirement for the exemption. The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which held that appellant retailers were not exempt from the payment of state motor fuel tax collected by appellee State of Kansas Department of Revenue. The court held that, although appellants were Indians, they were not exempt because Indian reservations within boundaries of the state were not included as territories outside the boundaries of the state, a statutory requirement for exemption.

 

16 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Board of Educ. v. Kansas State Bd. of Educ.


No. 80,000


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


266 Kan. 75; 966 P.2d 68; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 655



October 30, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court; FRANKLIN R. THEIS, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a civil suit, appellant State Board of Education (Kansas) sought review of the order of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas) upholding the constitutionality of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 72-8230(a)(as amended 1987).


OVERVIEW: The school district asserted that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 72-8230 (as amended)(1987) unlawfully impairs its right to unilaterally terminate its participation in an interlocal cooperative agreement with 15 other school districts. The § 72-8230 extended an interlocal agreement between the districts that terminated by its own terms in 1989. The school district argued that the amended statute violated both the United States and Kansas Constitutions. In the absence of significant impairment, the court would not find a violation of the Contract Clause. Further, the school district failed to show that the amendment allowed the state board to usurp the power granted to it by the Kansas Constitution. The state board did not have the authority to automatically reject a request to withdraw, but had to conduct a hearing whereby opposing sides may present evidence on behalf of their case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

17 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Canaan


No. 76,921


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


265 Kan. 835; 964 P.2d 681; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 407



July 24, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Canaan v. Bartee, 272 Kan. 720, 35 P.3d 841, 2001 Kan. LEXIS 941 (2001)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Canaan v. State, 2008 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 302 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Johnson district court; WILLIAM A. CLEAVER, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with premeditated murder, aggravated robbery, and aggravated burglary. The jury found him guilty, and the Johnson District Court (Kansas) entered judgment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Law enforcement officers suspected that defendant had committed a murder and decided to follow his truck. Defendant tried to elude the officers, but had an accident. At the scene, an officer found a wallet outside the truck and saw another wallet inside the truck. The wallet inside the truck belonged to the murder victim. Defendant claimed that the removal of the wallet from the truck was an unlawful search, and that evidence subsequently obtained pursuant to search warrants was tainted. The court held that there was no unlawful search and that the evidence was admissible. The court ruled that (1) the officers had a reasonable suspicion justifying a stop because defendant was speeding; (2) no stop occurred because defendant had an accident; (3) the officer had a duty to ascertain the identity of the injured driver under Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 8-1611, 8-1612; (4) after the officer removed the victim's wallet in the performance of his duty, the victim's license was in plain view; (5) the subsequent search of the truck was a valid inventory search; and (6) because the warrantless search of the truck was not unlawful, the subsequent searches pursuant to search warrants were not tainted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court and upheld the convictions.

 

18 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carr


No. 77,951


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


265 Kan. 608; 963 P.2d 421; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 402



July 10, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 17, 1998.
Post-conviction proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Carr v. State, 2001 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 969 (Kan. Ct. App., Feb. 23, 2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Sedgwick district court, THOMAS E. MALONE, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which convicted her of first-degree felony murder in the death of her adopted three-year-old daughter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's child died head injuries. Defendant admitted to spanking and shaking the child because of her bad conduct, but she contended that the child became injured after she rolled off of the bed. She admitted that when she shook the child her head bobbed back and forth. The court affirmed the district court's judgment that convicted defendant of felony murder because one instance of abuse of a child was a proper underlying felony for a felony-murder conviction. Even though abuse of a child did not require the specific intent to injure, it did require general criminal intent. Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3609 was not unconstitutionally vague because the phrases "cruel beating" and "inflicting cruel and inhuman corporal punishment" were reasonably definite standards. The district court's instructions to the jury did not violate the rule of jury unanimity because unanimity was not required as to the means by which the crime was committed as long as substantial evidence supported each alternative means. There was sufficient evidence for the jury to conclude that defendant, cruelly beat, inflicted cruel and inhuman bodily punishment on, and shook the child as prohibited by § 21-3609.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

State ex rel. Tomasic v. Unified Gov't


No. 81,074


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


265 Kan. 779; 962 P.2d 543; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 386

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator county district attorney filed an original proceeding in quo warranto, seeking rulings concerning the proposed construction of an auto racetrack facility and related projects in the county. Respondent was the unified county and city government.


OVERVIEW: County district attorney sought rulings concerning the proposed construction of an auto racetrack facility and related projects in the county. The court held that the development of an auto racetrack facility was a valid public purpose for which bonds could be issued and for which eminent domain authority could be exercised. The court held that the inclusion of an auto racetrack facility in the definition of a "major tourism area" bore a rational relationship to the furtherance of the economic development of the state. The court held that the amendments allowing auto racetrack facility special obligation bonds to have a maximum maturity of 30 years did not violate equal protection. The court held that the legislature could authorize a 25 percent premium to be paid to homeowners whose land was condemned for the development of an auto racetrack. The court held that the unified county and city government had not purchased or otherwise acquired real property prior to the adoption of a redevelopment plan and relocation assistance plan.


OUTCOME: The court denied the county district attorney's petition for a writ of quo warranto.

Board of County Comm'rs v. Bankoff Oil Co.


No. 77,111


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


265 Kan. 525; 960 P.2d 1279; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 387; 140 Oil & Gas Rep. 422



July 10, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Ness district court; J. BYRON MEEKS, judge. Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 24 Kan. App. 2d 532, 949 P.2d 628 (1997).



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals reversing the district court is reversed. Judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner oil and gas lease holder, an oil company, appealed the decision of the Court of Appeals (Kansas), which reversed the decision of the trial court. The trial court held that the Board of Tax Appeals' (BOTA) reconsidered opinion valuing the lease holder's lease was correct and the lease holder was due a tax refund.


OVERVIEW: The lease holder challenged the assessment made by the BOTA as to an oil and gas lease of a well that was in decline. The trial court affirmed the BOTA's reconsidered opinion and determined that the lease holder was due a tax refund of ad valorem taxes it had paid on the lease. The appeals court reversed the trial court's decision. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the appeals court and affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that appeals court did not correctly consider post- January 1 production data in determining the decline in production of the leased wells. The guidelines set up for determining the valuation of oil and gas leases stated the data produced after January 1 of the assessment year was to be utilized in determining the ad valorem taxes. There was substantial evidence that justified the BOTA's decision, and none of the provisions of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 77-612(c) required reversal. The trial court correctly upheld The BOTA's reconsidered opinion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appeals court and affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

21 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


In re Tax Appeal of Alsop Sand Co.


No. 76,870


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


265 Kan. 510; 962 P.2d 435; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 401



July 10, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Board of Tax Appeals. Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 24 Kan. App. 2d 527, 948 P.2d 667 (1997).



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals reversing the Board of Tax Appeals is affirmed. Order of the Board of Tax Appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kansas), which concluded that certain parts of machinery and equipment were not exempt from taxation as "major components" of manufacturing machinery and equipment under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-3606(kk).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer appealed the Kansas Department of Revenue's (KDR) assessment of additional sales and use taxes on parts of machinery and equipment. The taxpayer contended that the items were exempt from taxation as "major components" of manufacturing machinery and equipment under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-3606(kk). The hearing officer disagreed, and the taxpayer appealed to the Board of Tax Appeals, which concluded that the items were exempt. KDR appealed to the court of appeals, which concluded that the items were not exempt. The taxpayer sought review of the judgment, and the court affirmed the reversal of the Board's order. The court concluded that the application of the rules of statutory construction to § 79-3606(kk)(2)(A) led to the conclusion that the legislature intended to exempt major, but not non-major, components of manufacturing machinery and equipment. KDR's easily applied test of the scope of "major" implemented the legislative intent and made the statute workable for the taxpayer as well as the enforcement agency. Section 79-3606(kk), as interpreted by the court of appeals, did not violate the Equal Protection Clauses of the Kansas and United States Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that reversed the Board's order and concluded that the taxpayer's items were not exempt.

 

22 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Scott


No. 75,684


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


265 Kan. 1; 961 P.2d 667; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 372



May 29, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court; MATTHEW J. DOWD, judge. Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in State v. Scott, 24 Kan. App. 2d 480, 947 P.2d 466 (1998).



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals is affirmed in part and reversed in part. Judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual battery in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 21-3301. The trial court sentenced the defendant to probation and ordered him to register as a sex offender pursuant to the Kansas Sex Offender Registration Act (KSORA), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-4901 et seq. Defendant appealed his sentence, and the Court of Appeals (Kansas) held that the public access provision of KSORA was unconstitutional. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the public access provision of the Kansas Sex Offender Registration Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-4901 et seq., constituted cruel and unusual punishment in violation of the Eighth Amendment to the U.S. Constitution and § 9 of the Kansas Constitution Bill of Rights. The court declared the public access portion of the KSORA to be constitutional. In so holding, the court found that 1) the appellate court erroneously included injury to reputation in its consideration of cruel and unusual punishment; 2) the appellate court improperly applied a three-prong test, designed to determine the constitutionality of the length of a sentence, to the KSORA; 3) the legislature was within its discretion in determining that public safety necessitated access to the KSORA information; 4) defendant was placed on notice that he would be subject to the public disclosure portion of the KSORA at the time of his plea of nolo contendere; 5) the public access provisions of the KSORA were not so inhumane as to constitute cruel and unusual punishment; and 6) the appellate court properly held that the KSORA did not violate double jeopardy principles.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's ruling that the KSORA did not constitute double jeopardy, but reversed the appellate court's decision that the KSORA constituted cruel and unusual punishment in violation of the United States and Kansas Constitutions. The court affirmed the holding of the trial court.

 

23 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. McKinney


No. 77,884


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


265 Kan. 104; 961 P.2d 1; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 403



May 29, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Crawford district court; DONALD R. NOLAND, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Crawford District Court (Kansas), which, based on a jury verdict, convicted him of premeditated first-degree murder and aggravated robbery in one incident and of robbery in another. Defendant was sentenced to a hard 40 sentence for the murder.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions and the hard 40 sentence imposed for the murder. The court held: (1) that the Kansas statutory scheme for determining competence to stand trial was constitutional and defendant was not deprived his constitutional right to due process; (2) that the trial court did not err when it did not instruct the jury on felony murder as the lesser included offense of premeditated murder because felony murder was not a lesser included offense; both felony murder and premeditated murder were murders in the first degree; (3) that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction of aggravated robbery because the undenied continuity of events established the essential elements of aggravated robbery; the evidence showed that the murder victim was subjected lethal bodily harm and his property was taken; (4) that notice of a rebuttal witness was not required; and (5) that the imposition of the hard 40 sentence for the premeditated murder was justified because the evidence showed that the victim was murdered in an especially heinous, atrocious or cruel manner, in that, the victim endured 20 puncture wounds, choking, and banging of his head.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and the hard 40 sentence imposed for the murder.

State v. Sims


No. 79,155


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


265 Kan. 166; 960 P.2d 1271; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 368



May 29, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at Sims v. State, 2002 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 396 (Kan. Ct. App., Dec. 6, 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Sims v. State, 59 P.3d 1061, 2002 Kan. App. LEXIS 1111 (Kan. Ct. App., 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Sims v. State, 215 P.3d 648, 2009 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 725 (Kan. Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court; DAVID W. KENNEDY, judge.
State v. Sims, 262 Kan. 165, 936 P.2d 779, 1997 Kan. LEXIS 60 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Reversed, by reason of the erroneous admission of evidence unless there appears of record objection to the evidence timely interposed and so stated as to make clear the specific ground of objection. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in the Sedgwick District Court for 1 count of first-degree felony murder, 2 counts of aggravated battery, and 1 count of criminal discharge of a firearm and his sentence of life in prison plus a consecutive 60 months.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of multiple offenses in connection with a drive by shooting in which he drove the vehicle while a co-defendant did the shooting. On appeal the court affirmed his convictions. Defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on self-defense because, even if the evidence was viewed in the light most favorable to defendant, there was no evidence at trial that defendant reasonably believed force was necessary to defend himself. The court rejected defendant's argument that he was entitled to reversal because evidence of gang affiliation, which was admitted, was not related to the crime charged, nor was it admitted to show a motive for the crimes charged. Defendant failed to object at trial and therefore the issue was not preserved for appeal. Defendant's conviction for felony murder did not merge with the underlying conviction of criminal discharge of a firearm. Defendant did not properly preserve his argument that his consecutive sentences for felony murder and criminal discharge of a firearm violated double jeopardy because it was raised for the first time on appeal. However, the argument was meritless because the two crimes had different elements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

State v. Becker


No. 79,440


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


264 Kan. 804; 958 P.2d 627; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 102



April 24, 1998, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a petition for a writ of mandamus ordering respondent trial judge to commit defendant to a state hospital pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3248(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant assaulted a nurse while he was a patient in a state mental hospital. The trial court acquitted defendant of the charges on the basis of his mental defect or disease under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3221. Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3428(1)(a) mandated that a defendant who had been acquitted under § 22-3221 be committed to a state security hospital for safekeeping and treatment. The trial judge found that defendant's case was unique because defendant had already been committed to the state hospital, and defendant's doctors had determined that he was no longer a danger to himself or others based upon a change in his medication. The trial judge made a judicial determination that defendant did not need to be hospitalized, and that the purpose of § 22-3428 had been satisfied. The State filed the instant petition seeking a writ ordering the trial judge to commit defendant to a state hospital. The court denied the writ. The court found that the trial judge had not abused his discretion in determining that defendant would not benefit from being recommitted to the hospital. There was sufficient evidence to sustain the finding that defendant was no longer a danger to himself or others.


OUTCOME: The court denied the State's petition for a writ ordering the trial judge to commit defendant to a state hospital.

 

26 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rollins


No. 75,383


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


264 Kan. 466; 957 P.2d 438; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 76



April 17, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Rollins, 1998 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 14 (Kan. Ct. App., Dec. 24, 1998)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Saline district court; DAVID S. KNUDSON, judge. Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 24 Kan. App. 2d 15, 941 P.2d 411 (1997).
State v. Rollins, 24 Kan. App. 2d 15, 941 P.2d 411, 1997 Kan. App. LEXIS 99 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals reversing the district court is reversed and the case is remanded to the Court of Appeals for determination of the remaining issues. Judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State petitioned for review of a judgment from the Kansas Court of Appeals, which overturned defendant's conviction for perjury. The court of appeals ruled that the jury needed to decide whether defendant's statements were material. The State argued that under Kansas' perjury statute, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3805(a) (1992 Supp.), materiality was a question of law to be decided by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of perjury. The judge had instructed the jury that defendant's statements were material. On appeal, the court of appeals, relying on a United States Supreme Court decision, reversed defendant's conviction. The court of appeals found that the trial judge's refusal to submit questions of materiality to the jury violated the federal constitutional right to have a jury determine every element of the crime charged. The State sought review to the Kansas Supreme Court. The court determined that materiality was not an element of the Kansas perjury statute, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3805(a) (1992 Supp.). Thus, it was not a question for the jury. Under the Kansas criminal perjury statute materiality was a question of law for the trial judge. In the federal system, the United States Supreme Court was free to interpret federal statutes, but Kansas's courts were charged with the interpretation of Kansas's statutes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals that had overturned defendant's perjury conviction and remanded for determination of the remaining issues.

State v. Hemby


No. 77,384


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


264 Kan. 542; 957 P.2d 428; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 82



April 17, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Hemby v. Hannigan, 117 F. Supp. 2d 1057, 2000 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 15148 (D. Kan., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court; GREGORY L. WALLER, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Sedgwick County District Court (Kansas), which convicted defendant of one count of rape and one count of aggravated criminal sodomy and sentenced defendant to a controlling sentence of 15 years to life. Defendant contended that he was denied a speedy trial, that an erroneous instruction was given, and that defendant received a longer sentence because defendant asserted the right to remain silent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant originally pled guilty to rape and aggravated criminal sodomy. After the convictions were set aside, defendant was tried and convicted of one count of rape and one count of aggravated criminal sodomy. The record showed that defendant was appointed counsel 51 days after the trial court received the mandate that ordered a new trial. Defendant was not returned to the county for trial until 18 days before trial, and met with appointed counsel the next day. Defendant's counsel sought a continuance and requested that it be charged against the State. The continuance would have pushed defendant past the 90-day speedy trial deadline. The trial court also instructed the jury that sodomy included both types of oral copulation and did not require unanimity on the type of oral copulation. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that: (1) the trial court did not err when it charged the continuance against defendant and not the State; (2) unanimity as to the type of oral copulation was not required; and (3) the trial court considered the proper factors in sentencing and did not violate defendant's right to remain silent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of one count of rape and one count of aggravated criminal sodomy and sentence of a controlling sentence of 15 years to life.

State v. Mims


No. 76,580


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


264 Kan. 506; 956 P.2d 1337; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 83



April 17, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Mims v. State, 2005 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 308 (Kan. Ct. App., July 1, 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Mims v. Roberts, 2013 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 95 (Kan. Ct. App., Feb. 1, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wyandotte district court; J. DEXTER BURDETTE, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant directly appealed a judgment from the Wyandotte District Court (Kansas), which convicted defendant of felony murder, aggravated robbery, conspiracy to commit aggravated robbery, and aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and others participated in a crime spree that resulted in the robbery of a motel and the fatal shooting of the desk clerk by a co-conspirator. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence of other crimes to establish the events of the night in which the charged crimes occurred, to corroborate testimony, and to establish the parties' relationship and participation. The evidence was part and parcel of the crimes charged. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to allow defendant to inform the jury that he had already been convicted of conspiracy and aggravated assault in the first trial, as an attempt to utilize the result of his previous trial to indicate he should not be found guilty of the charges on which the first jury was unable to reach a verdict was not relevant. The trial court properly excluded evidence of witnesses' gang membership. Reading a vicarious liability instruction during voir dire, after jury selection, and at the close of the case was not error. Defendant's convictions for felony murder and aggravated robbery did not violate principles of double jeopardy, as they involved different elements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In re Vanderblomen


No. 79,424


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


264 Kan. 676; 956 P.2d 1320; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 92



April 17, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court; FRANK J. YEOMAN, JR., judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian of the patient sought review of the judgment of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which determined that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 59-2946(f)(1) (1997) was constitutional and ordered the discharge of the patient from a mental hospital.


OVERVIEW: The patient was in a motorcycle accident and suffered a traumatic closed head injury. In an action brought by the guardian, the district court determined that the patient was mentally ill and had her involuntarily committed. The patient's condition was reviewed several times by the district court, and it was determined that she suffered from an organic mental disorder. The patient's commitment continued until the enactment of § 59-2946(f)(1). The district court released the patient after it concluded that § 59-2946(f)(1) was constitutional and that it excluded persons suffering from organic mental disorder from involuntary commitment. On appeal, the court concluded that the district court's analysis of the statute was correct. Although the prevailing clinical guidelines no longer distinguished between organic and nonorganic mental disorders, the legislature had the right to make distinctions based upon the treatability of a condition. The legislature clearly intended to use the terms organic mental disorder as it had been previously and commonly used throughout the psychiatric community. Section 59-2946(f)(1) was not void for vagueness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that the statute was constitutional and that the patient should have been released from the mental hospital.

Legislative Coordinating Council v. Stanley


No. 79,533


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


264 Kan. 690; 957 P.2d 379; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 91



April 17, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised May 7, 1998.
As Amended May 8, 1998.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Legislative Coordinating Council (LCC) filed an original action for writ of mandamus against respondents Secretary of the Department of Administration and Director of Accounts and Reports (appropriation officials) to order them to pay vouchers the LCC submitted for court costs and attorney fees in an election contest for a seat in the Kansas House of Representatives.


OVERVIEW: The LCC was a board made up of the leadership of the Kansas House and Senate. In a contested election, the two candidates were required to appear before the legislature for a decision drawn by lots. Both parties were represented by counsel. The LCC requested that the state pay the costs and attorney fees, arguing the payments were a mandatory obligation of the state under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 25-1452. The payments were refused. The LCC brought this action to compel payment. The appropriation officials contested the writ, arguing the debts were illegal because payment of the LCC's vouchers would violate campaign finance laws and Kan. Const. art. 2, § 24, which required a specific appropriation. The court found the costs for insuring the ballots were accurately counted were appropriate expenses under § 25-1452, but that attorney's fees were not. The court next determined that, under §§ 25-1452 and Kan. Stat. Ann. § 25-1451 the attorney's fees were, according to the intent expressed by the legislature in its enabling legislation for the LCC, a valid obligation of the state. The payment for the LCC's vouchers, including the attorney's fees, did not require specific appropriations.


OUTCOME: The court granted the LCC's petition for a writ of mandamus.

Smith v. State


No. 78,509


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


264 Kan. 348; 955 P.2d 1293; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 72



March 13, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court; STEPHEN D. HILL, assigned judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrestees sought review of a judgment in favor of defendants, the State, a judicial district, and the 14 judicial district judges, from Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which granted defendants' motion to dismiss the arrestees' suit. The arrestees maintained that the own recognizance-cash deposit bond authorized by the rules of the judicial district violated the arrestees' constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The arrestees alleged that the pretrial release procedure, Third Judicial District Court Rule 3.311, was unconstitutional. Under the own recognizance-cash deposit bond provision, the judge set a bond amount. The arrestees were required to deposit 10 percent of that amount with the clerk of the district court. The arrestees received 90 percent of that deposit back upon completion of all obligations to the court--unless the arrestees had other financial obligations such as back child support or outstanding fines. If there were outstanding financial obligations, the $ 90 would be applied to those. Ten percent of the deposit would be kept as an administrative fee. The trial court dismissed the arrestees' suit pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-212(b)(1), (6). On appeal, the court affirmed and held: (1) there was no statutory authority for one district court to sit in judgment of a coequal district court; (2) the arrestees had other relief available through a motion to reduce bond or file a writ of habeas corpus; (3) the arrestees failed to show irreparable harm to justify equitable relief; and (4) the judges were immune from liability for judicial functions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that dismissed the arrestees' suit against defendants.

Citizens' Util. Ratepayer Bd. v. State Corp. Comm'n

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kansas), which invalidated certain portions of the Kansas Telecommunications Act of 1996, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 66-2001 et seq. (1996) and the Kansas Corporation Commission orders implementing that act on grounds they were inconsistent with the Federal Telecommunications Act of 1996, and also inconsistent with certain provisions of Kansas law.


OVERVIEW: The lower court invalidated certain portions of the Kansas Telecommunications Act of 1996 (Kansas Act), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 66-2001 et seq. and the Kansas Corporation Commission (KCC) orders implementing that act on grounds they were inconsistent with the Federal Telecommunications Act of 1996, and also inconsistent with certain provisions of Kansas law. The lower court also held Kan. Stat. Ann. § 66-1,143(b) did not prevent the KCC from requiring wireless service providers to contribute to the Kansas Universal Service Fund (KUSF); wireless service providers were not given proper notice of the proceedings and a reasonable opportunity to prepare for the hearings before the KCC; and the legislature's authorization to the KCC to determine the appropriate level of funding contribution and regulation of the KUSF was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power to an administrative agency. The court held that the Kansas Act did not conflict with the KCC's statutory duty to regulate and ensure just and reasonable rates and charges to consumers. The court reversed the court of appeals in regard to the KUSF and reinstating the KCC orders. The court affirmed otherwise.

State v. Edwards


No. 77,966


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


264 Kan. 177; 955 P.2d 1276; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 56



March 6, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised March 24, 1998.
Post-conviction relief denied at Edwards v. State, 2000 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 158 (Kan. Ct. App., Oct. 20, 2000)
Post-conviction relief denied at Edwards v. State, 209 P.3d 764, 2009 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 465 (Kan. Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Shawnee district court, JAMES P. BUCHELE, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder, aggravated robbery, and conspiracy to possess hallucinogenic drugs with intent to sell. The trial court sentenced defendant to a controlling term of life plus 58 months in prison. The trial court denied defendant's pretrial motion to suppress a photographic lineup identification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose out of the murder and robbery of a small-time drug dealer. Affirming, the court found that defendant failed to preserve his objections to the photographic lineup because he did not object at trial and that no substantial likelihood of misidentification existed due to the reliability of the courtroom identifications, based upon the witnesses' opportunity to view the accused at the time of the crime, their degree of attention, the accuracy of their prior descriptions, their level of certainty, and the length of time between the crime and the confrontation. The court held that defendant did not establish a prima facie case under Batson because he failed to show that the juror was a member of a certain race. The court concluded that a witness's passing reference to defendant's invocation of his Miranda rights was harmless error. The court held that a conference between the trial court and counsel about a jury question was not a critical stage at which defendant's presence was required and that marijuana found in defendant's apartment five weeks after the murder was too remote to be part of the res gestae, but its admission into evidence was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and remanded for entry of a nunc pro tunc order to correct the journal entry of sentence.

 

34 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Tomasic v. Unified Gov't of Wyandotte County


No. 80,223


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


264 Kan. 293; 955 P.2d 1136; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 48



March 6, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As revised April 1, 1998.



DISPOSITION: Quo warranto denied. K.S.A. 1997 Supp. 12-340 et seq. is upheld as constitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator district attorney filed a quo warranto petition seeking to have Kan. Stat. Ann. § 12-340 (1997) declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The action was filed by the district attorney seeking a ruling on the constitutionality of the Consolidation Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 12-340 et seq., which authorized a procedure whereby the voters of the county could adopt a consolidated government for the county and the city. Based on the distinction between a private group and a public administrative agency, the district attorney contended that the commission was a private group, as opposed to a public agency or board. The unified government argued that the commission was not an independently existing private association, but was a public administrative agency, created by statute, which the legislature properly delegated power to. The court denied the district attorney's petition for quo warranto. The court held that the commission was a public administrative agency. The commission was created by the legislature, to do as the legislature ordered. It was organized for the exclusive legislative purpose of preparing a plan to consolidate the two governments, with its powers prescribed by statute. Thus, the court concluded that it did not exist prior to or independent of legislative authorization.


OUTCOME: The court denied the district attorney's petition in quo warranto and upheld the statute as constitutional.

 

35 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. St. Francis Reg'l Med. Ctr.


No. 77,848


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


264 Kan. 144; 955 P.2d 1169; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 59



March 6, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court; MICHAEL CORRIGAN, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sedgwick District Court (Kansas) ruled that documents gathered and produced by the state board of nursing in connection with its investigation of decedent's death were protected by statutory privileges. Appellant parents and estate administrators took an interlocutory appeal from the district court's decision. The issues were whether the board documents were privileged and whether Kans. Stat. Ann. 65-1135(a) (Supp. 1997) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Decedent died from a ruptured ectopic pregnancy. The parents alleged that the emergency room nurse, who initially assessed decedent's condition, did not recognize its seriousness and did not alert a physician to the need for immediate attention. The hospital's first motion sought a protective order limiting use of documents obtained by the parents' counsel from the board relative to its investigation of the emergency nurse. The court held that although the interest in creating a statutory peer review privilege was strong, it was outweighed by the fundamental right of the parents to have access to all the relevant facts. The district court's protective order and order granting other discovery relief denied the parents that access and thus violated their right to due process and a fair determination of their malpractice action against the hospital and doctor. The information generated by the peer review committee, detailing the committee's decision-making process, was not subject to discovery by the parents. Forms and documents containing factual accounts and witnesses' names were not protected simply because they also contained the committee's conclusions or decision-making process.


OUTCOME: The district court's protective orders were reversed. The district court was directed to proceed to craft a protective order that would permit the parents' access to the relevant facts. The district court could simply redact that which was protected. The statute was presumed to be constitutional.

 

36 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lewis


No. 75,375


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


263 Kan. 843; 953 P.2d 1016; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 22



January 30, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised February 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wyandotte district court, THOMAS L. BOEDING, judge. Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 23 Kan. App. 2d 758, 935 P.2d 1072 (1997).
State v. Lewis, 23 Kan. App. 2d 758, 935 P.2d 1072, 1997 Kan. App. LEXIS 63 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirming the district court is reversed. Judgment of the district court is reversed, and the case is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Court of Appeals (Kansas), which affirmed her conviction of driving while a habitual violator under Kan. Stat. Ann § 8-287 (Supp. 1996), a severity level 9, nonperson felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a trial court of driving while a habitual violator under Kan. Stat. Ann § 8-287 (Supp. 1996), a severity level 9, nonperson felony. Defendant denied receiving the mailed notice of her license revocation as a habitual violator. The court of appeals concluded that the offense did not require that a licensee have actual knowledge of the notice declaring him or her a habitual violator, and thus, it affirmed the conviction. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction, remanded the case to the trial court, and held that knowledge of license status is an essential element of the offense of driving while a habitual violator, pursuant to § 8-287. The court concluded: (1) that knowledge of the notice was required in felony cases; (2) that there was no irrebutable presumption under notification procedures for habitual violators; (3) that the notice provisions of § 8-255(d) contained within the habitual violator statutes satisfied due process requirements; and (4) that there was no clear indication that the legislature in its amendment of the statute intended to dispense with knowledge of the license status as an essential element of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of driving while a habitual violator and remanded the case to the trial court.

 

37 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


In re Care & Treatment of Hay


No. 74,112


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


263 Kan. 822; 953 P.2d 666; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 24



January 30, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised February 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Johnson district court; PETER V. RUDDICK, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Johnson District Court (Kansas), which found that he was a sexually violent predator and ordered him to involuntary civil confinement pursuant to the Kansas Sexually Violent Predator Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 59-29a01 et seq.


OVERVIEW: After numerous convictions for sexual offenses, appellant was adjudicated a sexually violent predator and was ordered to involuntary civil confinement pursuant to the Kansas Sexually Violent Predator Act (act), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 59-29a01 et seq. Appellant sought review of the order and raised issues pertaining to the constitutionality of the act. The court rejected appellant's arguments and held that the act's definition of "mental abnormality" satisfied substantive Due Process requirements. The court also held that double jeopardy and ex post facto claims failed because the act was not criminal in nature. The court found that the act satisfied procedural Due Process requirements because the act provided for all the necessary basic protections such as appointed counsel, probable cause hearing, appointment of qualified experts for examinations, a jury trial requiring a unanimous decision, appeals, annual examinations, discharge petitions, hearings, and the strictest possible burden of proof on the state. The court held that the act did not violate equal protection because all members of the class of persons appellant was a part of were subject to identical treatment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's civil confinement pursuant to the Kansas Sexually Violent Predator Act (act) because the act was constitutional. The court held that the act was constitutional because it satisfied substantive and procedural Due Process requirements, was civil rather than criminal in nature, and did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because it treated all predators identically.

State v. Spain


No. 78,001


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


263 Kan. 708; 953 P.2d 1004; 1998 Kan. LEXIS 11



January 23, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised February 6 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Haskell district court; T. KEITH WILSON, judge.



DISPOSITION: Sentence vacated and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Haskell District Court (Kansas), which imposed a hard 40 sentence upon defendant after he entered a plea to one count of premeditated first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two other inmates fled the county jail after defendant shot the dispatcher. Defendant challenged his hard 40 sentence. The trial court found two aggravating circumstances and one non-statutory mitigating one. The court remanded for resentencing because the trial court erred in finding that the risk of death to a Colorado man who was kidnapped after the escape was an aggravating circumstance under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4636(b). The court found that any danger posed to the man was not sufficiently tied to the jailer's murder. The court held that the standard of proof for aggravating circumstances under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4635(c) was preponderance of the evidence and that the trial court properly found that defendant killed the jailer to avoid prosecution for the crime for which he was in jail, even though he had already entered into a plea agreement on that charge. The court concluded that age was not a mitigating circumstance in every case and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by rejecting defendant's other non-statutory mitigating factors, including lax operation of the county jail, defendant's lack of violent prior convictions, and his remorse.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded for resentencing.

Nance v. Harvey County


No. 75,703


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


263 Kan. 542; 952 P.2d 411; 1997 Kan. LEXIS 184



December 30, 1997, Opinion Filed
