State v. LaMunyon


No. 71,985


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


259 Kan. 54; 911 P.2d 151; 1996 Kan. LEXIS 10



January 26, 1996, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 21 Kan. App. 2d 281, 898 P.2d 1182 (1995). Appeal from Reno district court; WILLIAM F. LYLE, JR., judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. Judgment of the district court is affirmed in part, and the case is remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of possession of marijuana with intent to sell, sought review of a judgment from the Kansas Court of Appeals, which ruled that defendant's prior juvenile adjudications could be used in calculating his criminal history score under the Kansas Sentencing Guidelines Act.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's criminal history included four juvenile adjudications, one of which was for burglary. Before the effective date of the sentencing guidelines, defendant, then an adult, pleaded nolo contendere to possession of marijuana with intent to sell and was sentenced to incarceration. The trial court ruled that defendant was not eligible for retroactive sentence conversion because of the juvenile adjudication for burglary, and the appellate court affirmed. The court found no error, holding that the requirement that juvenile adjudications be considered in calculating an offender's criminal history score did not conflict with the statement in Kan. Stat. Ann. § 38-1601 that a juvenile adjudication was not to be deemed or held to import a criminal act. Although there was no right to a jury trial in juvenile proceedings, consideration of juvenile adjudications did not violate defendant's due process rights. Moreover, consideration of juvenile adjudications did not violate the prohibition against ex post facto laws because defendant's ineligibility for sentence conversion was not a punishment for his prior juvenile adjudications but was a consequence of his repeat offender status.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Wright


No. 73,507


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


259 Kan. 117; 911 P.2d 166; 1996 Kan. LEXIS 6



January 26, 1996, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 6, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Rooks district court, GLENN D. SCHIFFNER, assigned judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a pretrial motion to dismiss the grand jury's true bill of indictment. The Rooks District Court (Kansas) dismissed five counts that were written in statutory language for insufficiency because they lacked sufficient detail as to the specific criminal conduct involved. The dismissed counts charged defendant with criminal threat, stalking, harassment by telephone, and misdemeanor theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendant moved to dismiss the indictment without first moving for a bill of particulars. The State urged on appeal that the five dismissed counts were sufficient because they clearly charged each element of each offense and were phrased in the words of the applicable statute. Reversing as to four of the five counts, the court held that defendant was obligated to request a bill of particulars under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3201(f) (Supp. 1994) before asking for dismissal of counts that were drawn in the language of the statute and were legally sufficient under § 22-3201(b) and Kan. Const. Bill Rights § 10. The court found that a requirement that defendant knew his or her threat would be communicated to the person terrorized was not an element of the offense of criminal threat under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3419 (Supp. 1994) and that it was sufficient if there was an intent to terrorize or an act in reckless disregard of causing such terror. The court affirmed the dismissal of the stalking count because the indictment charged a violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3438 (Supp. 1994), which was unconstitutional and was not in effect when some of the charged conduct occurred.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of four of the five counts. The court affirmed the dismissal of the stalking count on the grounds that the indictment attempted to charge a violation of a statute that was not in effect when the behavior occurred and was unconstitutional.

 

84 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bryan


No. 73,978


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


259 Kan. 143; 910 P.2d 212; 1996 Kan. LEXIS 3



January 26, 1996, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Douglas district court, JACK A. MURPHY, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment from the Douglas District Court (Kansas) holding that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3438 (Supp. 1994) was unconstitutionally vague and dismissing a stalking charge against defendant. The trial court held that the terms "annoys" and "harasses," as used in the statute, were unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a relationship with the alleged victim. After the relationship ended, the alleged victim reported that defendant made repeated contacts with her. He was charged with one count of stalking. On appeal, the court found that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. Section 21-3438 contained no guidelines to determine when a following became alarming, annoying or harassing. There was no definition of the terms alarming, annoying or harassing in relation to an objective standard when a charge of stalking was based upon "following." Thus, that portion of the statute proscribing the intentional and malicious following when such following seriously alarmed, annoyed or harassed the person made the statute unconstitutionally vague. In the absence of an objective standard, the terms annoys, alarms, and harasses subjected defendant to the particular sensibilities of the individual victim. Persons of common intelligence must necessarily have guessed at the statute's meaning and differed as to its application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court.

Mobil Exploration & Producing U.S. v. State Corp. Comm'n


No. 72,895


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


258 Kan. 796; 908 P.2d 1276; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 166



December 15, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court, TERRY L. BULLOCK, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant gas companies sought review in a consolidated appeal from a judgment of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas) that affirmed the 1994 amendments issued by appellee Kansas Corporation Commission's (KCC) to the Basic Proration Order (BPO) controlling a certain gas field in Kansas.


OVERVIEW: The KCC's 1994 amendments to the BPO arose out of an application made on the basis that the BPO was not fulfilling its statutory mandates. The amendments were affirmed by the district court and affirmed by the court on appeal. The Natural Gas Conservation Act, Ken. Gen. Stat. § 55-701 et seq. (1935), empowered the KCC to prevent waste, avoid uncompensated drainage, and assure orderly development and production of natural gas in Kansas. The court stated that there was sufficient evidence to support the acreage factor amendment and that the KCC was statutorily authorized to make such an amendment under Kan. Stat. Ann. m 55-703(a). Further, though cross-examination on this issue was restricted, the complaining corporation was not deprived of its due process rights because the amendment was based only upon evidence that had been subject to cross-examination. Further, the KCC did not err by limiting a well's allowable to its demonstrated capacity to produce, by expanding the time allotted to produce existing underage, or by allowing certain pipeline companies to intervene in the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Ponce


No. 72,871


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


258 Kan. 708; 907 P.2d 876; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 150



December 8, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Norton district court, CHARLES E. WORDEN, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed, pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3602 (1994), an order from the Norton District Court (Kansas), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the pending charge of trafficking in contraband in a correctional institution, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3826 (1994), on the ground that it was a constitutionally impermissible delegation of legislative authority. The pending charge of possession of marijuana was dismissed without prejudice.


OVERVIEW: Section 21-3826 provided "contraband" was any item that was brought into a correctional facility without the consent of the facility's administrator. Section 21-3826 replaced a prior statute that provided a "laundry list" of contraband. The trial court sustained defendant's argument on the ground that § 21-3826 violated the separation of powers doctrine by giving the administrator unfettered discretion in the determination of what constituted contraband. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's contention that the trial court's dismissal of the marijuana charge deprived the court of jurisdiction. The marijuana charge was dismissed to allow the appeal of the trafficking charge. The court examined the legislative purpose of the statutes that delegated power to prison officials, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 75-5201 et seq., and held that the "laundry list" from the prior statute was insufficient. The administrator had a legitimate interest in prohibiting dangerous items in the facility, and normal items could be dangerous in the facility. The administrator's authority to promulgate and publish facility rules was not arbitrary or capricious. Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3826 was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the trafficking charge, held that the statute was constitutional, and remanded the trafficking charge against defendant for further proceedings.

National Council on Compensation Ins. v. Todd


No. 73,250


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


258 Kan. 535; 905 P.2d 114; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 137



November 3, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court; FRED S. JACKSON, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Kansas Department of Insurance (KID) challenged a judgment of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which found in favor of appellee National Council on Compensation Insurance (NCCI) in the NCCI's action alleging that Kan. Admin. R. § 40-3-50, a regulation promulgated by KID, exceeded the statutory authority of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-1117 and constituted a public taking without just compensation, in violation of the U. S. Constitution.


OVERVIEW: NCCI raised fees charged to insureds or agents requesting its worksheets on workers' compensation premium rates. KID promulgated Kan. Admin. R. 40-3-50 with the intent that NCCI should bear all costs associated with producing, and delivering their ratings worksheets to any insured or agent. A trial court found that Kan. Admin. Regs. 40-3-50 exceeded KID's statutory authority under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-1117 and that the regulation was in violation of U.S. Const. Amend. V and XIV as a taking without just compensation. A district court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3422, could not be read in isolation but could only be considered in connection with the other provisions of the Health Care Provider Insurance Availability Act (Act), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3401 et seq. There was no legislative intent that NCCI be required to furnish the information to an unlimited number of agents wishing to solicit an insured's business and to pass that cost on to all persons purchasing workers compensation insurance in this state through increased workers compensation premiums. The remaining issues were moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of NCCI.

Aves by & ex rel. Aves v. Shah


No. 73,184


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


258 Kan. 506; 906 P.2d 642; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 136



November 3, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification of two questions of law from the United States District Court for the District of Kansas, PATRICK F. KELLY, judge.



DISPOSITION: The questions certified are determined.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States District Court for the District of Kansas certified the following questions to the court: did Kansas law recognize a claim of bad faith against defendant Health Care Stabilization Fund (fund) when a judgment was returned in excess of statutory liability limits, and could plaintiffs, injured minor and her parents, prosecute such a bad faith action against the fund by way of garnishment pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-723(d)?


OVERVIEW: An injured minor and her parents, brought a medical malpractice action against defendants, a doctor and a hospital. The judgment against the doctor was seven times the limit of her insurance obtained through the fund. The injured minor and her parents brought a garnishment action in federal court against the fund for the fund's bad faith conduction of the doctor's defense and in failing to settle the claim. The federal court certified the following questions to the court: did Kansas law recognize a claim of bad faith against defendant Health Care Stabilization Fund (fund) when a judgment was returned in excess of the fund's statutory liability limits, and could the injured prosecute such a bad faith action against the fund by way of garnishment in light of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-723(d)? The court held that Kansas law did not recognize a claim against the fund for bad faith and refusal to settle. The court found that regarding due process, the availability of insurance for all Kansas doctors through the fund was an acceptable quid pro quo. The court held that the answer to the second question, due to its first answer, was moot.


OUTCOME: The answers to the certified questions are: (1) Kansas law did not recognize a claim of bad faith against the fund for a judgment in excess of the fund's statutory limit of liability, and (2) as a result of the answer to question one, question two was moot. The court found the availability of malpractice insurance for all doctors from the fund was an acceptable quid pro quo for due process concerns.

 

89 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


In the Interest of M.M.L.


No. 73,049


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


258 Kan. 254; 900 P.2d 813; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 115



July 21, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Barton district court, MIKE KEELEY, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant natural father challenged an order of the Barton District Court (Kansas), which placed appellee minor child of the father in long-term foster care at the request of appellee State of Kansas.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's order placed the father's minor child in long-term foster care upon the State's application. The father argued that the best interests of the child standard of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 38-1563(d) violated his constitutional right to custody of his child absent a finding of unfitness. The State argued that the father's fundamental constitutional rights had to give way to the best interests of the child test. The court stated that a parent who was not found to be unfit had a fundamental right, protected under the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution, to the care, custody, and control of his or her child, and that a parent's right to custody of a child could not be taken away in favor of a third person absent a finding of unfitness on the part of the parent. The court construed the best interest of the child language of § 38-1563(d) to be constitutional when applied in a child in need of care case when the trial court found by clear and convincing evidence that the parent was unfit or that highly unusual or extraordinary circumstances existed which substantially endangered the child's welfare. Absent such findings the parental preference doctrine controlled.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

90 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Delacruz


No. 71,969


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


258 Kan. 129; 899 P.2d 1042; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 110



July 14, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Seward district court, TOM R. SMITH, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the enhanced sentence imposed by the Seward District Court (Kansas) after he pleaded guilty to a charge of selling marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's criminal history sheet stated that he had three misdemeanor battery convictions. Pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4711(a), the convictions were treated as a felony conviction for criminal history purposes. The criminal history sheet also stated that he had three misdemeanor convictions for driving while suspended, the third of which was treated as a felony under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 8-262. Based on the two felonies, defendant received an enhanced sentence. On appeal, the court remanded the matter for further sentencing proceedings. The court determined that an uncounseled misdemeanor conviction that resulted in incarceration could not be used in determining the criminal history, absent a showing by the state that the right to counsel was waived. The court then noted that defendant was jailed on one of the battery convictions and that the record was silent as to whether he was represented by counsel. The court found that the conviction could not be used for criminal history purposes if defendant was not represented and the state failed to show that he waived counsel. The court also found that defendant could not collaterally attack the remaining misdemeanor convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and remanded the matter for further sentencing proceedings.

Ussery v. Kansas Dep't of Social & Rehabilitation Servs.


No. 72,324


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


258 Kan. 187; 899 P.2d 461; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 106



July 14, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Kiowa district court; DANIEL L. LOVE, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Kansas Department of Social and Rehabilitation Services (SRS) sought review of a judgment from the Kiowa District Court (Kansas) finding that appellant Medicaid claimant was entitled to a deduction of his court-ordered support obligation for his ex-wife from his available income, which affected the claimant's patient liability for his nursing home costs. On its own motion, the court transferred the appeal from the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: The claimant's only source of income was Social Security. The claimant was required to make monthly maintenance payments to his former spouse. Due to his health, the claimant was placed in a nursing home. He applied for Medicaid benefits. The SRS determined that the claimant was eligible and calculated his patient liability. The total of his patient liability and his monthly maintenance payments exceeded his available income. The claimant sought to have his monthly maintenance payments excluded from his available income. The SRS refused. The district court found that the SRS had erred. On appeal, the court interpreted the applicable regulations found at Kan. Admin. Regs. 30-6-106(m)(2) (Supp. 1993) that provided for an income allowance for a community spouse to be deducted from the income of an institutionalized spouse. The court looked to the plain, unambiguous language of the regulation and held that Kan. Admin. Regs. 30-6-106(m)(2) granted an allowance only to a "community spouse." It granted no similar allowance to an ex-spouse, nor did any other provision grant a similar allowance to an ex-spouse.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment and remanded the action.

State v. Alford


No. 71,633


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


257 Kan. 830; 896 P.2d 1059; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 83



June 2, 1995, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Sub nomine at State v. Duke, 263 Kan. 193, 946 P.2d 1375, 1997 Kan. LEXIS 153 (1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at Alford v. State, 221 P.3d 642, 2010 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 7 (Kan. Ct. App., 2010)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Alford v. Cline, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 50306 (D. Kan., May 10, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court, CLARK V. OWENS II, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which convicted him of first degree murder, aggravated kidnapping, and unlawful possession of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed his girlfriend and was convicted of first degree murder, aggravated kidnapping, and unlawful possession of a firearm. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that upon imposition of a hard 40 sentence, the phrase "automatic review" under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4627(1) (Supp. 1992) required that review had to be given even though defendant failed to properly follow the normal procedural rules for perfecting an appeal. Thus, the court had jurisdiction to hear the appeal. The jury's determination that the murder was committed in an especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel manner was supported by substantial competent evidence. Defendant chased the victim to the lobby of a restaurant, shot her twice, forced her into the kitchen and when she tried to flee, shot her again. As she was barely able to move yet still trying to escape, he, after a long series of clicks from his jammed gun, administered the final two bullets. A statement by the victim of an earlier aggravated battery was properly admitted because it was admissible to show that defendant was distraught over their breakup and had bearing on his intent to kill the victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

93 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gulledge


No. 72,315


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


257 Kan. 915; 896 P.2d 378; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 88



June 2, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Ellsworth district court, HERB ROHLEDER, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State sought review of an order of the Ellsworth District Court (Kansas), which dismissed a complaint against defendant for possession of marijuana and possession of marijuana without a tax stamp. The district court found that further prosecution of the complaint would have constituted double jeopardy because a drug tax had already been assessed and partially satisfied.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to the order of the district court dismissing the State's complaint against defendant, the State appealed. Upon review of the case, the court examined whether the assessment and payment of amounts allegedly owed under the Kansas Drug Tax Act constituted a criminal punishment for double jeopardy purposes. The United States Supreme Court had previously held that that tax on the possession of illegal drugs assessed after the State had imposed criminal penalty for the same conduct constituted a second punishment in violation of the Double Jeopardy Clause. Reversing and remanding the district court's judgment, the court held that the Kansas Drug Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-5201 et seq. did not consist of the "unusual feature" of a Montana tax which based its tax on the commission of a crime and that the taxpayer was still in possession of the property when the tax was imposed. In Montana the tax was imposed after the contraband had been confiscated. The court noted that § 79-5201 et seq. did not impose a criminal penalty on defendant because the revenue collection did not expressly depend on the illegal nature of the sale or possession of marijuana.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the district court's judgment.

State v. Gideon


No. 71,412


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


257 Kan. 591; 894 P.2d 850; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 63



April 28, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Cherokee district court; DAVID F. BREWSTER, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences entered in the Cherokee District Court (Kansas). Defendant was found guilty of premeditated first-degree murder, aggravated kidnapping, aggravated criminal sodomy, and rape. He received a hard 40 sentence for the murder and upward departure durational sentences on the other crimes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant kidnapped, sodomized, raped, and killed a female co-worker after the two had been at a party for a mutual friend. Defendant was convicted of premeditated first-degree murder, aggravated kidnapping, aggravated criminal sodomy, and rape. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and sentences. The court held that defendant had no right to have a jury decide whether he received the hard 40 sentence because he waived a jury determination of his guilt. A specific waiver by defendant on the record of the right to a jury determination of the hard 40 sentence issue was not required when defendant pled guilty to first-degree murder and was subject to the hard 40 sentence. The state gave notice of its intention to seek the hard 40 sentence as required under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4624(1) (1993) but was not required to give notice of the evidence it would use as aggravating factors. Defendant's confession was validly obtained and properly admitted. The departure sentences were properly imposed, and defendant received the notice he was due under the law. The reasons the trial court gave for the departures were substantial and compelling.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

City of Wichita v. Basgall


No. 72,105


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


257 Kan. 631; 894 P.2d 876; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 64; 4 Am. Disabilities Cas. (BNA) 533



April 28, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court, D. KEITH ANDERSON, judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The City appealed from a judgment of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), by which the district court upheld the trial court's determination that defendants were not guilty of improperly parking in areas adjacent to handicapped parking spaces in violation of Wichita, Kan., Code § 11.52.020(25)(b). The district court held that the spaces in which defendants parked were not properly marked and that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendants each parked a motorcycle in a department store parking lot in an area adjacent to a properly marked handicapped parking space. The areas where defendants parked were triangular and painted in yellow striped patterns. Each defendant was ticketed for parking in the access area of a handicapped parking space in violation of § 11.52.020(25)(b). The trial court and the district court held that the access areas were not marked in conformance with Kan. Stat. Ann. § 8-1,128 (1992) and the Americans With Disabilities Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 12101 et seq., and that the definition of access area in Wichita, Kan., Code § 11.52.020(25)(b) was impermissibly vague. On further review of the questions reserved pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3602(b)(3), the court held that the ordinance did not conflict with the statutes but permissibly enlarged upon their requirements for handicapped parking spaces. The court held that the definition of access area contained in Wichita, Kan., Code § 11.52.020(25)(b) was not impermissibly vague because a person of ordinary intelligence would have been aware that parking in a clearly marked space adjacent to a duly marked handicapped space was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the City's appeal on the questions reserved.

State v. Randall


No. 71,136


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


257 Kan. 482; 894 P.2d 196; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 55



April 21, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wyandotte district court; BILL D. ROBINSON, JR., judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and K.S.A. 60-1507 motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Wyandotte District Court (Kansas), which dismissed defendant's pro se motion for a conversion to a guideline sentence under the retroactivity provision of the Kansas Sentencing Guidelines Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. 21-4701 (1994 Supp.) et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed the trial court's dismissal of defendant's pro se motion for conversion to a guideline sentence under the retroactivity provision of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4701 (1994 Supp.), on the ground that it did not have jurisdiction to review the motion as defendant should have sought relief under Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 60-1507 or 60-1501. Defendant appealed asserting that the trial court should have construed the motion liberally and exercised jurisdiction. The court held that mislabeled pro se motions for sentence conversion under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4724(d) could be properly viewed as Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-1507 motions. Where district courts overlooked the jurisdictional issue entirely, appellate courts could review the merits as if the district court properly exercised jurisdiction under § 60-1507. In cases like defendant's, where the district court dismissed for lack of jurisdiction and where defendant's substantive contention raised purely a question of law, a remand was unnecessary. Therefore, the district court incorrectly dismissed for lack of jurisdiction. Defendant's motion was to be construed as one under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-1507.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and denied the motion.

Hixon v. Lario Enters.


No. 70,346


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


257 Kan. 377; 892 P.2d 507; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 46



March 22, 1995, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 19 Kan. App. 2d 643, 875 P.2d 297 (1994). Appeal from Shawnee district court, FRED S. JACKSON, judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals reversing the district court is affirmed as modified. Judgment of the district court is reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee real estate developer sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kansas), which reversed the district court and held that the developer's discount method of valuing subdivision property for ad valorem tax purposes was unconstitutional and violative of the Kansas statutory scheme of valuation under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-1439(a) (1994 Supp.). The court granted review because the issue was one of first impression in Kansas.


OVERVIEW: The real estate developer purchased two subdivisions that contained five categories of property, including vacant lots, rental property and dilapidated residences. The county appraised the property and the developer was successful in its appeal to the Board of Tax Appeals. The Board approved the developer's discount method. The district court concluded that the discount method was a lawful technique for valuing unsold subdivision properties. The appellate court reversed and held that the method violated the uniform and equal basis of valuation required under the state constitution. On appeal, the court held that the method violated the requirements of § 79-1439(a), which required that all real estate be appraised at its fair market value as defined in Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-503a. The court noted that a discount method had been approved with regard to unplatted raw ground that was slated for development, but such a method did not apply to a developed subdivision where the lots were marked and streets, curbs, and utilities were in place. The fair market value for a lot in such a subdivision already incorporated the costs of subdivision and the holding costs associated with raw land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate judgment, with modifications. It did not address the constitutional issue. It reversed and remanded the matter to the district court judgment with directions that it remand to the Board for further proceedings.

 

98 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Resolution Trust Corp. v. Fleischer


No. 72,429


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


257 Kan. 360; 892 P.2d 497; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 45



March 17, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification of two questions of law from the United States District Court for the District of Kansas, JOHN W. LUNGSTRUM, judge.



DISPOSITION: The questions certified are determined.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trust corporation filed an action in the United States District Court for the District of Kansas, asserting state law claims of negligence and breach of fiduciary duty against defendant savings association. The supreme court certified two questions of law concerning the constitutionality of retroactive legislation, which affected accrued tort actions.


OVERVIEW: Kan. Stat. Ann. § 17-5831 (Supp. 1994) essentially overruled the existing common law in Kansas under which "outside" directors of savings and loan associations could be held liable for negligence and breach of fiduciary duty. The legislature subsequently passed Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 9-1133, 9-1134 (Supp. 1994), which made Kan. Stat. Ann. § 17-5831 (Supp. 1994) applicable to any action that had not been finally adjudicated when § 17-5831 took effect. Several defendants therefore moved for summary judgment. The trust corporation claimed that it had a vested property right under Kansas law in its accrued tort causes of action, and that a retroactive application of § 17-5381 would violate Kan. Const. Bill Rights § 18. The savings association argued that an accrued cause of action was not a vested property right because it was inchoate and afforded no definite or enforceable property right until reduced to final judgment. The court held that the accrual right was a present right that had value, even if not easily measured in dollars. The court ruled that Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 9-1133, 9-1134 (Supp. 1994) violated due process and, therefore, violated Kan. Const. Bill Rights § 18.


OUTCOME: The court answered both certified questions and concluded that the weight of authority rested with the trust corporation. Under Kansas law, its accrued common-law causes of action for negligence and negligent breach of fiduciary duty, which had not yet been reduced to judgment, were "vested property rights." Further, the court determined that Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 9-1133, 9-1134 (Supp. 1994) was unconstitutional under the Kansas Constitution.

State v. Solomon


No. 70,831


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


257 Kan. 212; 891 P.2d 407; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 30



March 10, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Reno district court, WILLIAM F. LYLE, JR., judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Reno District Court (Kansas), which denied his motion to withdraw his plea of no contest to possession of cocaine with intent to sell within 1,000 feet of a school, and which gave defendant the maximum sentence of 15 years to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was on parole from Oklahoma at the time of the plea. In exchange for the plea, the State dropped all other charges against defendant. Affirming, the court said that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that the defendant's plea was voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently given and that the motion to withdraw the plea had to be denied. The court said that the plea was knowingly and voluntarily made. Defendant was informed that, by changing his plea, he waived his right to be presumed innocent, his right to a jury trial, and his right to appeal from a jury conviction. Defendant's arguments that his plea was not voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently given because he had not been advised of his privilege against self-incrimination and his right to confront his accusers were not properly before the court. The arguments had never been raised in the trial court. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing the maximum sentence. There was no contention that the sentence was the result of partiality, prejudice, oppression, or corrupt motive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to withdraw the plea and the sentence.

State v. Mountjoy


Nos. 70,586; 70,587; 70,588


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


257 Kan. 163; 891 P.2d 376; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 38



March 10, 1995, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended. As Corrected March 17, 1995. Second Correction April 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Johnson district court; WILLIAM A. CLEAVER, judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the Johnson District Court (Kansas), which entered judgment in favor of defendants after a jury found them not guilty of the charges of practicing the healing arts without a license under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 65-2803, a class B misdemeanor.


OVERVIEW: The State, pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3602(b)(3) (Supp. 1994), challenged the judgment on a question reserved by the prosecution and questioned whether the trial court erred by instructing the jury that criminal intent was a required element of the crime of practicing the healing arts without a license. During the trial, the prosecution objected to the trial court's jury instructions and informed the trial court that it wanted to reserve the question of the proof of intent. The court noted that the only question of importance raised by the State was whether the State must prove that the accused had the general intent to violate Kan. Stat. Ann. § 65-2803. The right to practice the healing arts was a privilege granted by legislative authority and not a natural right of individuals. The court held that the purpose of § 65-2803 was to protect the public. The public welfare doctrine provided that there was an exception for public welfare offenses regarding the common law rule that required the element of criminal intent. Therefore, the unauthorized practice of the healing arts was an offense that under the public welfare doctrine did not require the element of criminal intent.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the State's appeal.

 

101 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Stephan v. Parrish


No. 72,135


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


257 Kan. 294; 891 P.2d 445; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 35



March 10, 1995, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ of mandamus granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney general brought an original action in mandamus and quo warranto against respondents, the Secretary of the Kansas Department of Revenue and the Kansas Director of Property Valuation. At issue was the constitutionality of S.B. 542, § 14, 1994 Leg. (Kan. 1994), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-1427c (1994) and whether it violated the uniform and equal taxation provision of Kan. Const. art. 11, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The attorney general argued that S.B. 542, § 14, 1994 Leg. (Kan. 1994) was a retroactive property tax exemption, which created an improper or preferential classification of property in violation of Kan. Const. Art. 11, § 1, which provided for uniform and equal taxation. It was argued that the newly created tax exemption treated similarly situated taxpayers differently. The court granted the writ of mandamus, held that § 14 was unconstitutional, and severed it from the remainder of the statute. The court determined that § 14 was an unreasonable grant of a tax amnesty or "window of opportunity" based solely on a characteristic or status of the taxpayer rather than upon appropriate classification of the property. Taxpayers were divided into two classes, those who honestly reported their property for taxation and those who did not report their property for taxation or underreported the property if returned. The latter group was granted freedom from taxation and statutory penalties, while the former group was not. Such discrimination, when judged against the taxation guidelines, was arbitrary and lacked the rational basis necessary to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus in the attorney's action asserting that a statutory section violated the constitutional provision for uniform and equal taxation. The court concluded that the unconstitutional section was separate and independent from the remainder of the statute, and the court severed the unconstitutional section.

 

102 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gibbons


No. 70,249


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 951; 889 P.2d 772; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 19



February 3, 1995, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Gibbons, 1996 Kan. Unpub. LEXIS 34 (Kan., July 12, 1996)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Labette district court; CHARLES J. SELL, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Labette District Court (Kansas) after he was convicted of attempted first-degree murder, pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-330-1 (Supp. 1991), and possession of a concealed weapon, pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4201(d).


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot at the victim, who was having an extramarital affair with defendant's wife, several times. On appeal from his convictions, defendant contended, among other things, that the district court erred in failing to give the jury a lesser-included offense instruction, that the prosecutor's closing argument remarks prejudiced his right to a fair trial, and that he was improperly sentenced under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4618 (Supp. 1991). In affirming the judgment in part, the court held that a lesser-included offense instruction was not warranted because there was no substantial evidence that the lesser offense of an impulse killing had been committed; defendant had armed himself, waited for the victim, and shot at him numerous times. The prosecutor's closing argument remarks, which implied that defendant would commit further crimes if acquitted, were improper, but they did not prejudice defendant because he did not deny that he shot the victim. In reversing the judgment in part, the court held that defendant was improperly sentenced under § 21-4618 because attempted murder was not a crime set out in Chapter 21 of Article 34 of the Kansas Statutes Annotated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in part with regard to defendant's sentence under the firearms statute. The court affirmed the judgment in all other respects.

 

103 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Van Winkle


No. 70,514


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 890; 889 P.2d 749; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 6



January 27, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Geary district court; GEORGE F. SCOTT, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Geary District Court (Kansas) that revoked her probation in connection with her felony conviction for possession of cocaine and refused to reduce her life sentence, on her motion under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4603(4) (1991 Supp.). The State challenged the district court's jurisdiction to hear successive motions for revocation of probation and to modify a life sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was granted probation on the condition, inter alia, that she submit herself to a certain treatment program in Colorado. Before her entry into the program, the trial court revoked her probation for various violations. Defendant filed a motion under § 21-4603(4) and, after her probation was reinstated, she entered the treatment program. Defendant's probation was revoked when she left the program without permission of the court, allegedly because she was barred from attending church. The trial court revoked her probation. Defendant filed another § 21-4603(4) motion, which was denied. On appeal, the court rejected the State's claim that the trial court lacked jurisdiction over defendant successive petitions, holding that there were no statutory limitations as to the number of grants of probation that could be granted to a defendant. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in revoking her probation because the program was selected by defendant, her attendance was a condition to which she agreed, and the alleged unconstitutional condition was not specifically imposed by the trial court. Under §§ 21-4603(4)(a), (b), the trial court could not reduce defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

104 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Sedlak v. Dick


No. 70,792


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 779; 887 P.2d 1119; 1995 Kan. LEXIS 4



January 13, 1995, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original action in mandamus and quo warranto.



DISPOSITION: Writ of mandamus granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimants filed an original action for mandamus or quo warranto, challenging the constitutionality of Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 44-55b and 44-556. These sections dealt with the appointment and powers of the Kansas Workers' Compensation Board, as well as matters of judicial review of Board decisions. Respondents were the Kansas Secretary of Human Resources, the Kansas Director of Workers' Compensation, and the Board.


OVERVIEW: The claimants questioned the constitutionality of the legislature's action in establishing the Board, whose members were selected by representatives of private organizations, in eliminating the district court review of decisions concerning compensation of injured and disabled workers, and in limiting the review of the court of appeals to questions of law. The statutes in question were Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 44-555b and 4-556. The claimants alleged that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-555b violated the doctrine of separation of powers by authorizing the legislature to usurp the executive power to appoint executive officers. The court held that the power of appointment was not exclusively executive. The fatal flaw in Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-555b was not that private entities participated in the selection process, but that they selected the Board. The provisions of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-555b violated Kan. Const. art. 2, § 1 and were an impermissible delegation of legislative authority. Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 44-551 and 44-556 were not severable from Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-555b. All other provisions of the Kansas Workers' Compensation Act remained intact.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus sought by the claimants and they were entitled to a judgment ousting the members of the Board and dissolving the Board.

 

105 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Duke


No. 70,130


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 703; 887 P.2d 110; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 173



December 22, 1994, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Duke, 263 Kan. 193, 946 P.2d 1375, 1997 Kan. LEXIS 153 (1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at Duke v. State, 2006 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 590 (Kan. Ct. App., Nov. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court. DAVID W. KENNEDY, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas) that rendered judgment upon a jury verdict convicting defendant of first-degree murder, aggravated robbery, arson, and unlawful possession of a weapon. Defendant also appealed the imposition of the hard 40 sentence.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was arrested and being transported to a detention facility, another officer asked the escorting officer what he had, and the escort replied that he had a murder suspect. To this statement, defendant replied that he did it. Defendant's statement was later admitted into evidence. On appeal, defendant contended inter alia that his statement was not voluntary. The court ruled that there was substantial evidence to support the lower court's finding of voluntariness. The court held that: (1) defendant's statement was properly admitted because it was a voluntary and spontaneous utterance not urged by the officers; (2) the lower court did not give the jury permission to convict defendant under both alternative theories of murder by simply instructing them that they could convict him under both theories; (3) although one of the jury instructions misstated the law, the error was a benefit rather than a detriment to defendant; and (4) the aggravated arson instruction which omitted the element concerning "building of another" was not clearly erroneous because the jury was instructed that it had to find the building was the victim's residence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the imposed sentence.

 

106 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Stephan v. Parrish


No. 71,105


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 746; 887 P.2d 127; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 174



December 22, 1994, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 17, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court, JAMES P. BUCHELE, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Attorney General sought review of a judgment of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which granted judgment in favor of appellee Secretary of the Kansas Department of Revenue and intervenor bingo lodges and held that the "instant bingo" statutes, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-4701 et seq., were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Attorney General initiated an action against the Secretary contending that the "instant bingo" statutes, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-4701 et seq., were unconstitutional. The bingo lodges intervened and contended that the statutes were not unconstitutional. The trial court granted judgment in favor of the Secretary and the lodges, and the Attorney General sought review. Kan. Const. art. 15, § 3 provided that lotteries and the sale of lottery tickets were forever prohibited. Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-4701(a) defined the game of bingo and authorized the playing of the game. The court held that the constitutionality of a statute was presumed and that all doubts were resolved in favor of the validity. The court further determined that, before the bingo statutes were to be stricken down, it must have clearly appeared that the statutes violated the constitution. The court held that, because the constitution prohibited bingos and gambling, the legislature was not permitted to authorize the playing of such games. The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded a judgment of the trial court and held that, because the constitution prohibited bingos and lotteries, the bingo statutes were unconstitutional.

State v. Alston


No. 70,390


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 571; 887 P.2d 681; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 170; 23 Media L. Rep. 1321



December 16, 1994, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Atchison district court; MAURICE P. O'KEEFE, JR., and PHILIP C. LACEY judges.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a newspaper and its publisher, appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Atchison County (Kansas), convicting them of indirect contempt of court for violating the district court's order not to publish information contained in the court record and discussed in open court concerning the criminal background of an accused awaiting trial and the fact of the district court's order.


OVERVIEW: The accused had been charged with two felonies and five misdemeanors resulting from a stop and search of his vehicle by a police officer. A district court services officer filed a bond screen report on the accused. That report was part of the public court file, and it listed the accused's aliases and his prior criminal record. Shortly after the accused's arrest, the newspaper published an article stating that he had been denied bail on the basis of his previous conviction for felony theft. A reporter acquired information for the article from the county attorney. Prior to trial, the accused successfully filed a motion in limine to prevent the State from discussing or introducing evidence of his prior record. The district court also ordered a reporter appearing at the hearing to not report the accused's criminal history or the fact that the district court prohibited publication. The court noted that the district court did not make the requisite findings to issue a valid sua sponte gag order. Other than the district court's speculation, there was no indication that pretrial publicity would have precluded the accused from obtaining a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment of conviction.

 

108 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Jenkins v. Amchem Prods.


No. 71,406


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 602; 886 P.2d 869; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 172; 40 ERC (BNA) 1032; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P14,153



December 16, 1994, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court; KARL W. FRIEDEL, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff consumer brought a products liability action against defendant manufactures alleging that their products caused his cancer. The Sedgwick District Court (Kansas) ruled that the consumer sufficiently showed a defect, but the Federal Insecticide, Fungicide & Rodenticide Act (FIFRA), 7 U.S.C.S. § 136 et seq., preempted his tort claims, and granted summary judgment for the manufacturers. The parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The consumer argued that the preemption doctrine did not apply to his common-law damages action. The court held that § 136v(b) of FIFRA preempted the consumer's state tort claims that imposed requirements for the labeling and packaging of the manufacturers' 2,4-D products in addition to or different from FIFRA labeling requirements. Because all failure to warn claims are preempted under FIFRA, the consumer had no claim that survived preemption. The court concluded that the FIFRA provision that preempted state law claims was constitutional, as preemption of state law damages actions was reasonably related to the legitimate interest of uniformity of pesticide labeling and packaging regulations. The court found that the trial court erred in ruling that the consumer's allegation that the manufactures' 2,4-D products caused cancer was sufficient to raise a claim of design defect. The consumer could not prevail on a strict liability design defect claim without identifying what aspect of the manufacturers' products was defectively designed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment granted for the manufacturers.

Galindo v. City of Coffeyville


No. 70,850


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 455; 885 P.2d 1246; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 157



December 9, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Montgomery district court; DAVID L. THOMPSON, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fireman sought review of a decision of the Montgomery District Court (Kansas), which entered judgment for appellee city in his action for breach of contract and for taking his property right without due process of law in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 by failing to pay the appropriate retirement pension.


OVERVIEW: The fireman was employed by the city for a period of over 24 years prior to his retirement and participated in the city's pension plan. A dispute developed over how his monthly pension benefit was calculated, so fireman filed suit against the city, alleging that the city was liable for breach of contract and for taking his property without due process of law in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The trial court found that the fireman's pension payment was at least equal to that required by Kan. Stat. Ann. § 13-14a08 and that the fireman failed to prove his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim. On appeal, the court noted that it was called upon to review the trial court's interpretation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 13-14a08 and the retirement contract to determine whether the trial court correctly determined the monthly pension due the fireman. The court found that under the fact of the case, the formula that the city ultimately decided on for calculating the fireman's monthly pension was a unilateral modification of the fireman's pension but that the change was a reasonable one. The court concluded that the change in the pension plan made by the city did not result in a disadvantage to the employee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision.

Sunflower Racing v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 70,316


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 426; 885 P.2d 1233; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 163



December 9, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wyandotte district court; R. DAVID LAMAR, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the judgment of the Wyandotte District Court (Kansas) that affirmed the decision of the Kansas State Board of Tax Appeals (BOTA) denying its tax protest and request for equalization of the appraised value of property for ad valorem purposes. Appellee board of county commissioners were parties to the action.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a facility offering both horse and dog racing, challenged its ad valorem tax assessment in the years shortly after it was constructed. BOTA conducted a hearing and upheld the assessment. BOTA then considered the motion for rehearing and affirmed its prior order, as did the district court. On appeal, the court noted that it had jurisdiction to review the BOTA determination under the Act for Judicial Review and Civil Enforcement of Agency Actions, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 74-2426(c). The court held that the taxpayer failed to sustain its burden of proving that BOTA's actions were invalid. The taxpayer waived its objection to the number of officers who conducted the hearing and participated in the decision. It did not object or request substitutes for the two members who failed to complete the hearing. Nor did the taxpayer show an arbitrary disregard of the undisputed evidence or some extrinsic consideration such as bias, passion, or prejudice. The assessment validly was made in reliance upon the cost method, considering actual construction costs, and did not vary greatly from the taxpayer's appraisal. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

111 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Unified Sch. Dist. No. 229 v. State


No. 70,931


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 232; 885 P.2d 1170; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 144



December 2, 1994, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court, MARLA J. LUCKERT, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, school districts, taxpayers, and students, filed an action challenging the constitutionality of the School District Finance and Quality Performance Act. The Shawnee District Court (Kansas) upheld the constitutionality of the act with the exception of its provisions regarding the low enrollment weighting factor in its classification scheme, and the school districts, taxpayers, and students filed an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted legislation requiring each local school board to levy a tax on property in its district, deposit the funds into its general fund, and remit any excess funds to the state for use in funding public education in poorer districts. The school districts, taxpayers, and students claimed that the act violated Kan Const. art. VI, § 6(b) because it did not make suitable financial provision for public education. They also claimed that the act's classification scheme violated the equal protection principles in Kan. Const. Bill of Rights § 1 and that the act's recapture provision violated the Takings Clause of U.S. Const. amend. V, XIV. The court held that the legislation was constitutional. In so holding, the court found that (1) the legislation made suitable provision for education under the standards set by the state department of education; (2) the classification scheme of the legislation was rationally related to legitimate state interests; and (3) the requirement that the wealthier districts remit excess funds to the state did not violate the Takings Clause because all taxpayers benefitted from the quality of the education received by students in the state.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's ruling that the act's provisions regarding the low enrollment weighting factor were unconstitutional, affirmed its ruling that the act was otherwise constitutional, and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

112 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Robinson


No. 70,111


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 133; 883 P.2d 764; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 130



October 28, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Robinson, 1996 Kan. Unpub. LEXIS 9 (Kan., Apr. 19, 1996)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wyandotte district court; PHILIP L. SIEVE, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Wyandotte District Court (Kansas), which, upon a jury verdict, convicted him of aggravated robbery and attempted first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The victim was shot several times after she was robbed. The State charged defendant with aggravated robbery and attempted first-degree murder. The trial court instructed the jury that it could convict defendant of attempted first-degree murder if it found the shooting was intentional, deliberate, premeditated, and with intent to kill, or if the shooting occurred during the commission or attempted commission of an aggravated robbery. The jury returned a general verdict of guilty to attempted first-degree murder (and aggravated robbery), but it did not indicate whether it relied on the premeditation or felony-murder theory. On appeal, the court held that the attempted felony-murder instruction was clearly erroneous because Kansas did not recognize attempted felony murder. Moreover, the attempted felony-murder instruction erroneously diminished the State's burden to prove a specific intent to kill required for attempted first-degree murder. The instruction and general verdict form did not require the jury to unanimously find defendant intended to commit premeditated murder. Thus, a legally erroneous ground for the conviction could have been the basis for the jury's finding of guilt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the attempted first-degree murder conviction and remanded for a new trial on that charge.

Rios v. Board of Pub. Utils.


No. 70,736


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 184; 883 P.2d 1177; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 133



October 28, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Workers Compensation Board.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On transfer from the Workers Compensation Board (Kansas), the claimant employee challenged the decision of an administrative law judge, which found, in favor of appellee city employer, that the employee suffered a 25 percent impairment as a result of his work-related injury. The case was transferred after the appellate court questioned the board's jurisdiction because the employee had filed to request a review of the ALJ's award by the board.


OVERVIEW: The injury occurred when the employee was struck in the back of his head and his neck by a large chunk of asphalt as he was working on a water main. The court reasoned that prior to an amendment to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-551, seeking review by the director was not a prerequisite to judicial review of the ALJ's award. However, the court held that § 44-551 was amended to provide that all acts, findings, awards, decisions, rulings, or modifications of findings or awards made by an ALJ were subject to review by the board upon written request of any interested party within 10 days, and if no such request was made, the board was required to approve the actions, findings, awards, decisions, rulings, or modifications of findings or awards of the ALJ. The court held that review by the board was a prerequisite to judicial review as provided for in § 44-556. Therefore, the court concluded that an appellate court had no jurisdiction to consider an appeal from an order of the board when no written request for review of the decision of the ALJ had been filed as required by Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-551.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

Corder v. Kansas Bd. of Healing Arts


No. 70,425


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


256 Kan. 638; 889 P.2d 1127; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 141



October 28, 1994, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Shawnee district court; FRANKLIN R. THEIS, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff physician sought review of an order from the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which upheld the suspension of his license and denied his claim for damages in his action against defendants, the Kansas Board of Healing Arts and its executive director. The Board challenged an order awarding attorney fees to the physician.


OVERVIEW: The Board entered an emergency order temporarily suspending the physician's license and directing him to submit to a mental examination. The emergency order was based upon psychiatric evidence concerning his ability to care for his patients. The central inquiry dealt with the physician's expressed beliefs concerning unidentified flying objects (UFOs) and extraterrestrial beings. The physician filed an action against defendants, seeking relief in the nature of a mandamus compelling the Board to afford him a hearing on the emergency suspension. The trial court upheld the suspension of the physician's license. The trial court denied the physician's claim for damages, but awarded him attorney fees against the Board. On appeal, the court found that the issuance of the emergency suspension order was consistent with both the provisions of the Kansas Healing Arts Act and the provisions of the Kansas Administrative Procedure Act. The court further found that the Board's denial of a hearing on the issue of suspension denied the physician due process of law. Finally, the court found that the trial court erred in awarding attorney fees to the physician on the mandamus claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order upholding the physician's suspension and denying his claim for damages. The court reversed the order awarding attorney fees to the physician.

116 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. Kansas Water Office


No. 70,196


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


255 Kan. 990; 881 P.2d 567; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 126; 9 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1705



September 22, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court; ADRIAN J. ALLEN, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state water office sought review of the decision of the Shawnee district court, which awarded appellee civil service employee damages and reinstatement pursuant to his wrongful termination claim.


OVERVIEW: Appellee civil service employee filed a wrongful termination claim against appellant state water office based upon a written contract 4 years and 122 days after his termination. The court held that the employment relationship between the state and appellee did not arise out of a written contract, but the relationship was fixed by statute. The court found that the focus of appellee's claim was that as a classified civil service employee, he held a right not to be terminated without a hearing and without good cause. The court found that he would not have had these rights but for the Kansas Civil Service Act (KCSA), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 75-2925 et seq. The court held that appellee's wrongful termination action clearly relied on the KCSA to provide the basis of liability he sought to impose on appellant. The court found that appellee's breach of employment contract claim was an action "upon a liability created by a statute" and consequently must have been filed within three years of his termination pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-512(2). The court reversed the decision of the trial court because appellee's claim was time barred.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court which found in favor of appellee civil service employee in his wrongful termination claim against appellant state water office because appellee's claim was time barred as it was an action upon a liability created by a statute, and should have been filed within three years of his termination.

 

117 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Boeing Co. v. Oaklawn Improvement Dist.


No. 69,863


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


255 Kan. 848; 877 P.2d 967; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 123



July 19, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court; C. ROBERT BELL, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a municipal improvement district, challenged the order of a Kansas trial court, which granted appellee corporate taxpayer's request for an injunction under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-907 to prohibit the levy, assessment, and collection of future taxes against the taxpayer's tangible property located within improvement district. The trial court had sua sponte declared unconstitutional the Improvement Districts Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 19-2753.


OVERVIEW: The corporate taxpayer was assessed a large portion of the overall bond amount necessary for the improvement district to expand and repair its sewer system, which had been approved by the voters. It paid one year's taxes and protested the next two years' levy. Its protests were before the Board of Tax Appeals when it instituted its suit for an injunction. The trial court declared the Act unconstitutional in part because the taxpayer, as the entity paying the largest portion of the assessments, did not receive notice and due process. It impounded the protested tax payments. On appeal, the court held that the Act was not constitutionally defective. It held that the notice required under the Fourteenth Amendment in a condemnation action was not applicable in a situation involving assessments. It noted that the taxpayer was not entitled to a freeze on the disbursement of the taxes it paid under protest. It held further that the taxpayer had not exhausted its administrative remedies before the Board with regard to its tax protests and the authority of the improvement district to assess its tangible property. The taxpayer's real property was exempt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and remanded with directions that it dissolve the injunction and dismiss the case.

 

118 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


In re City of Wichita


No. 70,358


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


255 Kan. 838; 877 P.2d 437; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 114



July 15, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court, CHARLES ANDREWS, JR., judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a judgment of the Shawnee County District Court (Kansas), which affirmed the denial of an exemption from ad valorem taxes on real estate owned by the city, acquired through civil forfeiture by law enforcement for drug law violations. Appellee Board of Tax Appeals denied the exemption.


OVERVIEW: The city held the real estate pursuant to criminal forfeitures for narcotics violations. The city did not gain revenue from the property until the property was sold. The profits were put into the police department's fund to fight narcotics. The court affirmed the judgment of the district court. The court held as follows: 1) the city was not entitled to the exemption because the property was not under "actual use" as required by Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-201a; 2) the city did not lease the property, and the property did not generate any revenue for the city during its ownership; 3) the city held title to the property, did not actually use the property, acquired revenue from the property, and used that revenue for a public purpose; and 4) the fact that the funds were from the sale were eventually used for a public purpose did not create an actual use of the property for purposes of the exemption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court affirming the board's denial of the exemption.

Lindenman v. Umscheid


No. 69,110


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


255 Kan. 610; 875 P.2d 964; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 97



June 3, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wyandotte district court; PHILIP L. SIEVE, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administrator of day care center challenged an order of the Wyandotte District Court (Kansas), that granted summary judgment to appellee department of health and environment regarding administrator's charges for abuse of process and malicious prosecution.


OVERVIEW: An administrator of a day care center filed an action against the department of health and environment, the city, and the county for violation of their civil rights, malicious prosecution, and abuse of process. The administrator alleged the department of health and environment was biased, prejudiced, and vindictive when they immediately suspended the day care's license. The trial court granted some of the department's motions for summary judgment and both parties appealed from the decision. The reviewing court found the administrator was precluded from bringing the action against the department and thus their cause of action for abuse of process was tolled. The department conceded the malicious prosecution claim was not barred by the statute of limitations. Finally, the reviewing court found the civil rights claim was proper because the governmental agency did not have a discretionary right to violate a legal duty and avoid liability. Thus the granting of summary judgment in favor of department on the abuse of process and malicious prosecution claims were reversed.


OUTCOME: The order granting summary judgment in favor of department on the abuse of process and malicious prosecution claims were reversed.

McVay v. Rich


No. 69,224


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


255 Kan. 371; 874 P.2d 641; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 74



May 27, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 18 Kan. App. 2d 746, 859 P.2d 399 (1993). Appeal from Shawnee district court; ADRIAN J. ALLEN, judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirming the district court is affirmed. Judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals (Kansas) affirming the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital. The court of appeals relied upon the Health Care Provider Insurance Availability Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3401 et seq., and Kan. Stat. Ann. 65-442(b), in rendering its decision in the medical malpractice cause of action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient challenged the decision affirming the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital in the medical malpractice cause of action. The patient alleged that the hospital was liable for damages because it permitted the surgeon to operate in its facilities. The court held that the hospital was statutorily protected from liability for damages arising from the negligence of the surgeon, who was an independent contractor, not an employee of the hospital. Kan. Stat. 65-442(b) eliminated health care facility liability for licensed surgeons who were not employees of the facility. Further, the Health Care Provider Insurance Availability Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3401 et seq., provided immunity to health care providers covered by the Health Care Stabilization Fund (Fund) from vicarious liability for damages arising from services rendered by other health care providers covered by the Fund. Because the surgeon and the facility both were covered by the Fund, the court found that the lower courts had properly dismissed the patient's cause of action against the hospital. Claims not raised earlier regarding the constitutionality of the provisions were rejected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision upholding the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital in the medical malpractice cause of action brought by appellant patient.

State v. Timley


No. 68,697


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


255 Kan. 286; 875 P.2d 242; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 82



May 27, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at Timley v. State, 1996 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 197 (Kan. Ct. App., Feb. 2, 1996)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Timley v. State, 1998 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 390 (Kan. Ct. App., Aug. 28, 1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at Timley v. State, 2001 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 940 (Kan. Ct. App., Apr. 20, 2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Timley v. Nelson, 36 Fed. Appx. 387, 2002 U.S. App. LEXIS 10500 (10th Cir. Kan., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick District court; DAVID W. KENNEDY, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which convicted him of three counts of rape and four counts of aggravated criminal sodomy stemming from three separate incidents involving three victims.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that each alleged victim approached him and agreed to perform sexual activity on him in exchange for drugs. Defendant admitted to choking each victim and making threats, but insisted that the choking was intended to be mutually sexually stimulating. Affirming the conviction, the court held that there was sufficient evidence that defendant was guilty of rape and aggravated criminal sodomy either by the means of force or the means of fear and that there was no error in including both alternatives in one jury instruction. Defendant was not denied his statutory speedy trial right, pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3402(1), because the continuances were properly charged to him. The State's use of two peremptory challenges to exclude males from the jury was proper because there were valid reasons other than gender that justified excusing the jurors. Defendant's rights were not prejudiced by permitting witnesses to testify even though they were not cross-endorsed. Identity was a contested issue at trial, so it was not error to admit prior crimes evidence. Defendant was given reasonable notice that the Habitual Criminal Act would be imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court.
