City of Wichita v. Lucero


No. 69,839


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


255 Kan. 437; 874 P.2d 1144; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 93



May 27, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court, PAUL W. CLARK, judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal sustained; case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The city appealed a judgment of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which ruled that the mandatory minimum fine provision for repeat offenders, like defendant, as set forth in Wichita, Kan., Code § 5.66.055(b), was unconstitutional in violation of defendant's rights under §§ 1 and 2 of the Bill of Rights of the Kansas Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for violating Wichita, Kan., Code § 5.66.055(a)(1), which prohibited intentional interference with or the obstruction of a lawful business, while participating in a pro-life demonstration at a women's clinic. A jury convicted defendant of violating the ordinance. The trial court held that the mandatory minimum fine provision of the ordinance for repeat offenders was unconstitutional. The court sustained the city's appeal, remanding the case with directions to resentence defendant. The court held that § 5.66.055 was not unconstitutional under the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the Bill of Rights of the Kansas Constitution and of the United States Constitution. The ordinance provided a sufficient alternative method of punishment, community service, as an alternative to the mandatory fine provision and was not unconstitutional as applied to indigents such as defendant. While the ordinance may have been imprecise, it gave a clear and sufficient warning as to the conduct proscribed. Because there was no evidence that the clinic was a public forum, defendant was not afforded First Amendment protections on the privately owned property.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the city's appeal and remanded the case with directions to resentence defendant.

Kerns by & Through Kerns v. G.A.C., Inc.


No. 68,405


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


255 Kan. 264; 875 P.2d 949; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 95



May 27, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 10, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court; D. KEITH ANDERSON, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff disabled minor appealed the order of the Sedgwick district court (Kansas), which granted summary judgment to defendants, operators of a park and fence company, and found defendant corporation two percent negligent in the disabled minor's action seeking damages for serious injuries sustained from nearly drowning in a swimming pool. The corporation cross-appealed the denial of its motions for summary judgment and directed verdict.


OVERVIEW: A disabled minor fell into a closed swimming pool at a mobile home park and nearly drowned. After he filed a lawsuit, the district court granted summary judgment to the park operators and the fence company, and the jury found the corporate owner of the park two percent negligent. On appeal, the court affirmed the summary judgment to the fence company because Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-3303(b)(1) barred the claim. Further, the fence company had no duty to warn because the danger or hazard was open or obvious and should have been realized by a reasonable user of the product. The court reversed the summary judgment to the operators because they had either assumed or assigned their duty to pump accumulated water from the pool to an agent of the corporation. They had a responsibility to act and failed to act, and they owed a duty to the disabled minor. The district court erred in admitting collateral source benefits evidence. The denial of the corporation's summary judgment and directed verdict motions was affirmed because the disabled minor's status as a trespasser did not preclude submission to the jury of the negligence per se claim based on two ordinances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the order of the district court, and remanded the matter for a new trial. The park operators were not entitled to summary judgment, but the fence company was entitled to summary judgment based on a statute of repose.

State v. Sodders


No. 68,931


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


255 Kan. 79; 872 P.2d 736; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 66



April 15, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended April 22, 1994. Second Correction May 25, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 18 Kan. App. 2d 657, 856 P.2d 1360 (1993). Appeal from Johnson district court, ROBERT G. JONES, judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirming the district court is affirmed. Judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Kansas, sought review of a decision by the Court of Appeals (Kansas) that affirmed the trial court's order in an interlocutory appeal challenging the trial court's granting of appellee defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence, finding that the police acted outside of their jurisdiction in executing the search warrant.


OVERVIEW: At the suppression hearing, it was undisputed that police officers from an outside city, executed a search warrant in the forum city without any request for assistance by the officers of the forum city. The state contended that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-2505, a statute specifically dealing with the execution of search warrants, was not limited by the general geographical limitations of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-401(a). The court ruled that § 22-401 was controlling. The court reasoned that while Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-2505 admittedly applied only to the execution of search warrants, the language of that statute simply could not be read as an exception to the clear geographic limitation set forth in Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-2401(a). The court reasoned that § 22-2401(a) as the later enacted statute prevailed. The court held that § 22-2401(a) was the more specific statute and that when there was a territorial limitation placed upon law enforcement officers, that limitation was controlling. The court concluded that the outside officers lacked jurisdiction because they failed to meet one of the two exceptions under § 22-2401, which would permit them to exercise power outside of their jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Whitaker

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court; CLARK V. OWENS II, judge.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed, sentences vacated, and case remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which convicted him of one count of aggravated robbery, two counts of kidnapping, one count of aggravated battery against a law enforcement officer, and one count of attempted aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions, vacated the sentences, and remanded for resentencing. The court was unable to determine from the sentencing transcript if the trial judge carefully considered, or failed to consider, the impact that defendant's false testimony had on his capacity for rehabilitation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions, vacated the sentences, and remanded for resentencing.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of a decision of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which entered judgment on a jury verdict for appellee hospital in the patient's negligence action which arose from treatment he received at the hospital for injuries sustained in an accident at his place of employment. The patient challenged the admissibility of evidence at trial under Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 60-453, 60-452.

Stat. Ann. §§ 60-452, 60-453. OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for a new trial.

In re Guardianship of Williams


No. 69,506


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


254 Kan. 814; 869 P.2d 661; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 44



March 4, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court; HAL MALONE, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner natural mother sought to terminate a voluntary guardianship established for her minor son and to have her son returned to her care. Respondent guardian opposed the mother's petition. The Sedgwick District Court (Kansas) denied the mother's petition. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: In denying the mother's petition, the trial court held that the mother had to show not only that she was fit, but also that the change of custody materially promoted the child's best interests and welfare. On appeal, the mother argued that the trial court applied the wrong legal standard. The appellate court agreed. Absent extraordinary circumstances, the best interests of the child test had no application in determining whether a parent, not found to be unfit, was entitled to custody as against a third-party nonparent. As the mother was not found unfit, she was entitled to the relief sought.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment denying the mother's petition to terminate the voluntary guardianship established for her minor son.

 

128 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Scherzer


No. 70,590


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


254 Kan. 926; 869 P.2d 729; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 46



March 4, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wyandotte district court; WILLIAM M. COOK, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for correction of sentence.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment from the Wyandotte District Court (Kansas), which allowed defendant to serve 90 days of imprisonment by home incarceration rather than the imprisonment that was required by Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3405b(b)(2) after defendant was convicted of vehicular battery in violation of § 21-3405b.


OVERVIEW: After defendant pleaded guilty to three counts of vehicular battery, he was fined and sentenced to one year of imprisonment on each count, with the sentences to be served concurrently. The district court ordered that defendant was to serve 90 days of imprisonment by home incarceration that was to be followed by probation because it determined that the penalty provision of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3405b constituted cruel and unusual punishment. The court reversed the district court's judgment. Section 21-3405b(b)(2) provided that a defendant was not eligible for probation until he served at least 90 days of imprisonment. Even though the home incarceration statute, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4603b, did not preclude imposing home incarceration for vehicular battery, a plain reading of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4603, which set forth sentencing options, listed imprisonment and home incarceration as two separate options. The penalty for vehicular battery required that defendant serve time in prison, not by home incarceration. Even though the misdemeanor penalties for § 21-3405b violations were harsher than those for some felonies, § 21-3405b did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment and remanded the action to the district court for the correction of the illegal sentence.

Chiles v. State


No. 70,018


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


254 Kan. 888; 869 P.2d 707; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 49



March 4, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action in mandamus and quo warranto.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed an original action in mandamus and quo warranto naming the State of Kansas as respondent. The inmate sought an order from the court requiring the State to apply to him the limited retroactivity provisions of the Kansas Sentencing Guidelines Act set forth in Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4724(b)(1) (Supp. 1993). The Act made eligibility for sentence conversion dependent upon the classification of less serious offenders.


OVERVIEW: The inmate did not fall within the Act and was not eligible to have his controlling sentence modified because of the severity level of his crime of aggravated robbery. He contended that his exclusion from the retroactivity provision of the Act was the result of an arbitrary classification which bore no relationship to the purpose of the retroactivity legislation and thus, violated equal protection. The court determined that as the dispositive question was whether the sentencing guidelines were unconstitutional, the appropriate review standard was whether there was a rational basis for the classification. Applying this standard, the court concluded that the limited retroactivity provision of the Act did not clearly violate the constitutional right to equal protection as there was no suspect class or fundamental right involved. The retroactivity provision was valid in that it was reasonably related to the legitimate objective of reducing prison population while maintaining public safety. The court also found that the limited retroactivity provision was reasonable in relation to its subject, was adopted in the interest of the community, and was not violative of due process.


OUTCOME: The court denied the inmate's petition for writ of mandamus and quo warranto.

State ex rel. Stephan v. Finney


No. 69,616


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


254 Kan. 632; 867 P.2d 1034; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 29



January 27, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action in mandamus and quo warranto.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is entered for the respondent in accordance with the opinion herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney general filed an original action in mandamus and quo warranto against respondent governor to determine if the governor was authorized under Kan. Const. art. 15, § 3c to negotiate compacts with Indian tribes that authorized casino gambling pursuant to the Indian Gaming Regulatory Act (IGRA), 25 U.S.C.S. § 2701 et seq. The governor removed the action to federal court. The federal court remanded the case.


OVERVIEW: The state senate passed a resolution requiring that the attorney general obtain a judicial determination of whether Kan. Const. art. 15, § 3 authorized the governor to negotiate compacts with Indian tribes that authorized casino gambling under the IGRA in light of the gambling prohibitions in Kansas. On remand from the federal court, the court determined that the federal court was the proper forum to address the federal questions involved the in claims under the IGRA and the Johnson Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 1171. The court found that the term "lottery" in Kan. Const. art 15, § 3 had provided a complete prohibition to well-defined forms of gambling. However, the court held that a reading of the legislative history prior to and subsequent to when art. 15, § 3c was enacted left no doubt that the legislature intended the advent of a state-owned and operated lottery, developed, organized, and operated to provide revenue and not limited to lotteries such as those functioning in other states. Thus, art. 15, § 3c was not self-executing and altered the broad definition of lottery previously expressed.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment for the governor, finding that the governor was authorized under the Kansas Constitution to negotiate compacts with Indian tribes that authorized casino gambling.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with official misconduct for advising potential witnesses to events involving defendant's son, who was under investigation. The court found that § 21-3902 was unconstitutional because it was susceptible to arbitrary and discriminating interpretation and application by those charged with the responsibility of enforcing it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In re Anr Pipeline Co.


No. 69,116


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


254 Kan. 534; 866 P.2d 1060; 1994 Kan. LEXIS 23



January 21, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied ANR Pipeline Co. v. Dir., Prop. Valuation, 513 U.S. 917, 115 S. Ct. 296, 130 L. Ed. 2d 209, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 6979 (1994)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Kansas Board of Tax Appeals.
Colorado Interstate Gas Co. v. Beshears, 18 Kan. App. 2d 814, 860 P.2d 56, 1993 Kan. App. LEXIS 113 (1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public utilities sought review of an order of the Kansas Board of Tax Appeals (BOTA), which upheld the decisions of the Director of Property Valuation (DPV) denying the public utilities' requests to have their properties assessed on the same bases as railroad property.


OVERVIEW: Congress enacted the Railroad Revitalization & Regulatory Reform Act of 1976, 49 U.S.C.S. § 11503 (4-R Act), to prohibit discriminatory taxation of railroad property by state and local tax laws. Litigation under the 4-R Act resulted in several consent decrees, one of which fixed the railroads' assessment rate for real property for 1990 and 1991. The public utilities sought to have their properties assessed on the same bases as railroad property for those years. The DPV and the BOTA denied the requests. On review, the court held that the BOTA order did not violate the uniform and equal provision of Kan. Const. art. 11, § 1(b) (amended 1992) where the 4-R Act preempted the state classification of railroads and where limiting the presumption of the 4-R Act to its purposes and application resulted in minimal interference with the classification system under Kan. Const. art. 11, § 1(b) (amended 1992). The court also held that the BOTA order did not violate equal protection where Kan. Const. art. 11, § 1(b) (amended 1992) treated all public utility property alike and where the 4-R Act preempted the classification only as to railroad property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the BOTA's order.

Smith v. Printup


No. 67,591


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


254 Kan. 315; 866 P.2d 985; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 188



December 30, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court, PAUL BUCHANAN, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, administrator and heirs, sought review of the decision of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which awarded punitive damages in a survivor action to the extent the appellee employee's conduct was authorized or ratified, pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-3703, and denied punitive damages in a wrongful death action. Appellee corporation and the employee filed cross-appeals.


OVERVIEW: A driver died instantly and her passenger died at the scene after a truck driven by the employee crossed the median and struck the driver's vehicle. The employee worked for appellee employer but had been "leased out" to the corporation for the prior four to five years. In the ensuing action, the jury did not access punitive damages against the employer, awarded punitive damages against the employee and the corporation in a survival action by the administrator, but denied punitive damages for the wrongful death actions. The court affirmed the constitutionality of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-3701 because a party had no vested right to punitive damages, and the legislature could modify the method of how punitive damages were determined. Further, a wrongful death action was a statutory creature, and Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-1901 did not contemplate punitive damages. The court reversed and remanded the lower court's punitive award decision and held that admissible and relevant evidence of the employer's and corporation's authorization and ratification conduct, which affected the substantial rights of the administrator and heirs, was improperly excluded by the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the punitive damages decision and remanded with instructions to determine whether punitive damages should be awarded against the employer and if awarded, the appropriate amount, and to determine the amount of punitive damages against the corporation and the employee. The court ordered the proper instruction on ratification and authorization and affirmed the remaining portion of the lower court's judgment.

State v. Willis


No. 68,445


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


254 Kan. 119; 864 P.2d 1198; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 169



December 10, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Reno district court; WILLIAM F. LYLE, JR., judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Reno District Court (Kansas) entered a judgment convicting defendant of premeditated first degree murder, in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3401. Defendant was sentenced to a mandatory 40-year term of imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After finding defendant guilty of the premeditated first degree murder of his wife, the jury found that defendant, under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4625(6), had committed the crime in an especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel manner. Defendant appealed, arguing that his absence during the pathologist's deposition violated his constitutional right of confrontation. He also argued that the aggravating circumstance, which formed the bases for his hard 40 sentence, was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court reversed on the witness confrontation issue and remanded the case for a new trial. The court held that the unavailability of the pathologist was not explicitly shown, that the basis for the trial court's declaration of unavailability was absent from the record, and that the reliability and trustworthiness of the deposition was in doubt because the pathologist did not sign the deposition. The court concluded that it was unable to determine beyond a reasonable doubt that the admission of the deposition testimony had little, if any, likelihood of changing the result at trial. The court also provided new instruction language for the hard 40 sentencing proceeding under § 21-4635(6).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

135 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Kenyon v. Kansas Power & Light Co.


No. 69,309


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


254 Kan. 287; 864 P.2d 1161; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 170



December 10, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Leavenworth district court, DAVID J. KING, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff alleged injured victim sought review of a judgment entered in the Leavenworth District Court (Kansas), that dismissed her personal injury action against defendant utility company by applying the provisions of the Overhead Power Line Accident Prevention Act, (OPLA), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 66-1701 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The injured victim filed a personal injury action to recover from injuries he incurred while working at the utility company's site. The trial court instructed the jury in accordance with the OPLA and the jury found in favor of the utility company. The injured victim argued on appeal, that application of OPLA was error because the legislation was improperly enacted under Kan. Const. art. 2, § 14 and therefore was void. The court agreed with the injured victim. The court pointed out that a bill never became law until the constitutional prerequisites pertaining to the manner of enactment had been fully complied with. The court noted that the version of OPLA that was signed by the governor was not the same version that was passed by both houses of the legislature, which violated Kan. Const. art. 2, § 14. The court also pointed out that it did not have the authority to change a statute to conform with a bill that the legislature had passed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

Bullock v. Whiteman


No. 68,678


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


254 Kan. 177; 865 P.2d 197; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 185



December 10, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court, M. KAY ROYSE, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, recipients of benefits under the General Assistance (GA) and Medikan programs, appealed from a decision of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which entered judgment in favor of defendant, Secretary of the Department of Social and Rehabilitation Services, in the recipients' suit that alleged the proposed narrowing of eligibility for GA benefits and reduction in Medikan benefits violated Kan. Const. art. 7, § 4 and equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The recipients filed a class action. The proposed regulations eliminated all Medikan benefits, reduced GA payments by $ 9 per month, and increased eligibility requirements. In affirming, the court held that the Secretary's action in seeking to eliminate cash and medical assistance to certain members of the recipients' class did not violate Kan. Const. art. 7, § 4. According to the court, the proposed changes were reasonably expected to be in furtherance of the optimum utilization of public assistance funds. The court noted that the new GA requirements provided a rough method of identifying those who were unable to provide for their own basic needs. The court also determined that the Secretary's action in seeking to eliminate or substantially reduce cash and medical assistance to certain members of the class did not violate the equal protection guarantees of the Kansas and United States Constitutions. The court noted that participation in the federal assistance programs did not require the State to grant the same level of benefits to needy persons not eligible for any of the federal programs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Board of County Comm'rs v. Graham


No. 69,199, No. 69,200


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


254 Kan. 260; 864 P.2d 1141; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 163



December 10, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court, PAUL BUCHANAN, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, the parties, plaintiff Board of County Commissioners and defendant landowners, challenged decisions from the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which rejected the Board's method of cost allocation and developed and adopted its own version of cost allocation under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-2803. The parties also challenged the district court's determination that certain costs should be included in the allocation.


OVERVIEW: In both actions, the Board sought to enforce tax liens on certain parcels of property. In each instance, the Board filed an order approving apportionment of costs, charges, and expenses. The orders set forth the Board's methodology of cost, expense, and balance allocation pursuant to § 79-2803. When the owners challenged the method of allocation, the district court developed its own version. In their cross-appeals, the owners argued that excessive and improper costs were included in the district court's allocation. The Board argued that the district court's allocation was inequitable. On review, the court determined that in both instances, the Board failed to show that the allocation method adopted by the court was contrary to § 79-2803. However, all filing and docketing fees paid in excess of $ 65 were improper and should not have been included in the allocation of costs because the petitions seeking tax foreclosure constituted one case for each of the owners. While the foreclosure was sought on multiple parcels, each petition constituted one case. Finally, it was proper for the district court to set aside the sale of one parcel because the owner was not properly served.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment in each case. The cases were remanded to the district court.

In re Appeal of Morton Thiokol, Inc.


No. 67,954


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


254 Kan. 23; 864 P.2d 1175; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 172



December 10, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Board of Tax Appeals of the State of Kansas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a decision of the Board of Tax Appeals of the State of Kansas, which upheld an addition to the corporation's state income tax as assessed by appellee Kansas Department of Revenue.


OVERVIEW: The additional tax resulted principally from the use of the domestic combination method of apportioning income and expenses for the corporation, which was multijurisdictional, and the treatment of foreign dividends as apportionable income. The corporation contended that it had been denied due process by the department's changing tax rules and policies without issuing regulations. The corporation further argued that the department's treatment of foreign dividends was improper because the dividends were treated under the domestic combination method, which was contrary to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-32,141 and Kan. Admin. Regs. 92-12-77. The court disagreed with the position taken by the corporation. The evidence showed that there was no change in the department's treatment of foreign dividends during the tax years that were in contention. Thus, the denial of due process claim was meritless. Additionally, the department's treatment of foreign dividends was proper because the Uniform Division of Income for Tax Purposes Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-3271 et seq., apportioned income, but it did not define the income base that was to be apportioned. Thus, the department was within its authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which upheld the addition to the corporation's tax.

Dickerson v. Kansas Dep't of Revenue


No. 67,693


Supreme Court of Kansas


253 Kan. 843; 863 P.2d 364; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 158



November 12, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in an unpublished decision filed November 25, 1992. Appeal from Crawford District Court; Nelson E. Toburen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirming the district court is affirmed. Judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant department sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Kansas), which affirmed a judgment that plaintiff taxpayer's plea bargain in a criminal drug case collaterally estopped a drug tax proceeding by the department to sell the taxpayer's car to collect the tax. The trial court enjoined the department from attempting to collect the tax and ordered the Sheriff to release the taxpayer's automobile.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was charged with possession of more than 28 grams of marijuana without a tax stamp and possession of marijuana. He made a plea bargain agreement and entered a plea of guilty. The trial court placed the taxpayer on probation and ordered him to pay taxes pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-5202 (1991 Supp.) and a fine of $ 350 pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-5208 (1991 Supp.). He paid the fine and the tax. The department issued a drug tax assessment against the taxpayer pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-5205(a) (1991 Supp.) and took possession of his car. The taxpayer brought an action against the department to enjoin it from collecting the tax. The trial court's judgment for the taxpayer was affirmed and the department sought further review. The court held that: (1) the plea agreement was binding and the department was collaterally estopped from collection of the tax; (2) pursuant to Kan. Sup. Ct. R. 141(b), 1992 Kan. Ct. R. Ann. 124, the taxpayer, in response to the department's summary judgment motion, did not have to controvert facts; and (3) exhaustion of administrative remedies was not required because the binding effect of the plea agreement took precedence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that enjoined the department from the collection of drug possession tax against the taxpayer and ordered the sheriff to return the taxpayer's automobile to him.

 

140 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


City of Overland Park v. McBride


No. 68,900


Supreme Court of Kansas


253 Kan. 774; 861 P.2d 1323; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 147



October 29, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Johnson District Court, John Anderson III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed from the Johnson District Court (Kansas), which dismissed its complaint charging defendant with unlawful possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the complaint because it failed to allege an essential element of the offense, which was intent. The question presented on appeal was whether the complaint was fatally defective by failing to specifically allege intent. The city asserted that defendant waived any objection to defects in the complaint because he did not raise them before trial. The court found this contention was without merit. The city also contended that Overland Park, Kan. Municipal Code § 11.56.140 (1986) created absolute liability for the offense of possession of marijuana. Thus, the city contended that there was no requirement that the complaint allege intent. The court found no legislative intent for the imposition of absolute liability in the adoption of the ordinance. However, the court found that possession of marijuana under the Overland Park Municipal Code was a general intent crime, and that the charging language of the ordinance was sufficient to state an offense. Thus, the court held that the trial court erred by dismissing the complaint on the basis that it failed to state an offense by omission of the word intent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the city's complaint.

Reed v. Kansas Racing Comm'n


No. 68,820


Supreme Court of Kansas


253 Kan. 602; 860 P.2d 684; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 136



October 8, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick District Court; William D. Rustin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant racetrack manager challenged a decision of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which affirmed an order of appellee, the Kansas Racing Commission. Pursuant to the Parimutuel Racing Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 74-8801 et seq., the Commission's order revoked the manager's occupation license, fined him, and permanently excluded him from the track.


OVERVIEW: The Commission found that the racetrack manager, who was involved in gambling activities, was not qualified to perform his duties under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 74-8816(e)(3), and had violated Kan. Admin. Regs. § 112-11-21(a) (1991) as effected by 18 U.S.C.S. § 1084(a), and Kan. Admin. Regs. § 112-11-21(j), (k) (1991). The Commission revoked his occupation license, fined him, and permanently excluded him from the track. The Commission's order was affirmed by the trial court. On appeal, the court affirmed the revocation of his license as it was supported by substantial evidence. The court also affirmed his exclusion from the track. The court held that the statutes and regulations were not unconstitutionally vague. However, the court concluded that the notice of the charges was insufficient and facially inadequate when compared to the regulatory violations found by the Commission, and the court vacated the order as it related to those violations and fines. As a matter of law, the Commission and the trial court had incorrectly applied the regulations in question to the facts of the case. The manager's conduct was not a violation of either of the regulations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the decision, which affirmed the Commission's order revoking the manager's occupation license and permanently excluding him from the track. The court also affirmed some of the fines imposed. However, the court reversed the part of the order, which found the manager had violated regulations prohibiting certain wagering and gambling, and vacated the fines imposed for those alleged violations.

 

142 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cromwell


No. 67,881


Supreme Court of Kansas


253 Kan. 495; 856 P.2d 1299; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 131



July 30, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick District Court, Clark V. Owens II, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of premeditated first-degree murder, two counts of aggravated robbery, two counts of rape, one count of aggravated criminal sodomy, and one count of theft. He appealed from the judgment of the Sedgwick County District Court (Kansas), arguing, inter alia, that his counsel was ineffective and his rights to self-representation and to be present at trial were denied.


OVERVIEW: The crimes involved two incidents in which mature women whom defendant knew were strangled to death in their apartments. There were no signs of forced entry and property was missing. In the first incident, the Deoxyribonucleic Acid (DNA) of seminal fluid matched defendant's DNA. In the second incident, there was not sufficient seminal fluid to conduct a DNA test, but defendant's hair was consistent with a hair found at the scene. The court held that defendant's counsel was not ineffective, despite the claim that there was a communication problem. Counsel and defendant frequently conferred with one another. Defendant's request to serve as co-counsel indicated that he did not want to represent himself; nor was he constitutionally entitled to serve as co-counsel. Defendant waived his right to be present at trial. His poor relationship with counsel did not render his absence involuntary. The motion to sever the charges was properly denied. The lapse of four years and the differing ages of the victims did not make the crimes dissimilar. Evidence of the first incident was admissible to establish identity in the second incident. The evidence supported the mandatory 40-year sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of two counts of premeditated first-degree murder, two counts of aggravated robbery, two counts of rape, one count of aggravated criminal sodomy, and one count of theft. The court also affirmed the sentence.

Cott v. Peppermint Twist Management Co.


No. 67,575


Supreme Court of Kansas


253 Kan. 452; 856 P.2d 906; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 128; 21 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 553



July 14, 1993, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by Cott v. Peppermint Twist Mgmt. Co., 1997 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 727 (Kan. Ct. App., Feb. 21, 1997)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee District Court; Matthew J. Dowd, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bar and appellee patrons sought review of a judgment of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas) that was in favor of appellees in their suit for personal injuries they received when they were negligently served dishwashing soap in their alcoholic drinks but that capped appellees' damages pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-19a02 (1992 Supp.).


OVERVIEW: Appellee patrons ordered watermelon shots while at appellant bar. Unbeknownst to appellees, the bucket containing the drink mix had negligently been filled with a dishwashing solution used in appellant's automatic dishwasher. When appellees' drank the substance, they suffered severe burns as a result of the lye in the solution. Appellees sued appellant for their injuries. A verdict was returned in appellees' favor, but the trial court applied a damages cap pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-19a02 (1992 Supp.). The trial court denied appellant's motion for a new trial. Both sides appealed, and the court affirmed. Appellant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence supporting the award of future medical expenses and future loss of income. When a verdict was attacked on the ground that it was contrary to the evidence, it was not the court's function to weight the evidence of pass on the credibility of the witnesses. Because the evidence, with all reasonable inferences to be drawn therefrom, when considered in the light most favorable to appellees, supported the verdict, the court would not disturb the verdict. There were also no grounds to impeach the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: Judgment that was in favor of appellee patrons in their suit against appellant bar for the personal injuries they received when they were negligently served dishwashing soap in their alcoholic drinks and that imposed a statutory damages cap on the award was affirmed. There was substantial evidence supporting the jury's award of future medical expenses and future lost income. There were no grounds upon which to impeach the verdict.

State ex rel. Stephan v. Kansas Dep't of Revenue


Nos. 68,703, 69,031, 69,291


Supreme Court of Kansas


253 Kan. 412; 856 P.2d 151; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 116



July 9, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee District Court; Terry L. Bullock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenors, the boards of county commissioners and county appraisers, sought review of an order from the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which denied intervenors the right to join in a lawsuit filed by plaintiff, the Attorney General of the State of Kansas, against defendants, the Kansas Department of Revenue and the Secretary of the Department, the Kansas Director of the Division of Property Valuation, and the Kansas State Treasurer.


OVERVIEW: The intervenors claimed that the trial court erred in denying their motions to intervene pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-224(a), because they had an interest in the outcome of the litigation that was filed by the Attorney General that was seeking a declaratory judgment and injunction to require defendants to not collect taxes until a uniform and equal fair market appraisal had been completed. The court held that the intervenors had failed to show that they had a substantial interest in the litigation, which was required by § 60-224(a), because under the provisions of Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 79-1401, 79-1403, and 79-1404 the Kansas Director of Property Valuation was responsible for the state wide supervision of the assessment, appraisal, and collection of property taxes and intervenors had not been ordered to do anything by the Director. The court further held that until such time as intervenors were required to comply with any requests by the Director, they were not considered interested parties in the outcome of the litigation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

City of Prairie Village v. Hogan


No. 68,733


Supreme Court of Kansas


253 Kan. 423; 855 P.2d 949; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 117



July 9, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Johnson District Court; Gerald L. Hougland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff City of Prairie Village (Kansas) charged defendant with picketing before or about a church in violation of Prairie Village, Kan., Ordinance 1785, art. 9.13. The Johnson District Court (Kansas) convicted defendant and imposed a fine, and defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant walked on a sidewalk across the street from a church and its two parking lots carrying antiabortion signs and testified that he was not picketing the church because his communication was not directed at the church but rather to all persons traversing the road. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred in construing Prairie Village, Kan., Ordinance 1785, art. 9.13 to apply to his conduct and that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The court held that it was required to uphold a statute if possible and narrowly construed the ordinance to prohibit only focused picketing taking place solely in front of a church. Defendant, who walked a route on the opposite side of the street and directed his message at all persons traversing the road, was not engaged in conduct prohibited by the ordinance. Because the ordinance did not apply to defendant's conduct, it was not necessary for the court to reach the challenge to the constitutionality of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of a judgment from the Marshall District Court (Kansas), which denied his petition for mandamus seeking an order compelling defendant employer to continue payment of the employee's salary pending the outcome of a due process hearing and any post-hearing appeals.


OVERVIEW: After the employer, a school district, gave the employee, a tenured teacher, notice of non-renewal of his teaching contract for the following school year, a due process hearing was held at the employee's request. The hearing committee found in favor of the employee and the employer filed an appeal with a trial court. The court held that the employee was entitled to continue to receive his salary until the date that the employer filed its notice of appeal with the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

 

147 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Jurado v. Popejoy Constr. Co.


No. 68,212


Supreme Court of Kansas


253 Kan. 116; 853 P.2d 669; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 90; 5 A.L.R. 2207; 28 A.L.R.5th 857



May 28, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Hamilton District Court, J. Stephen Nyswonger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee's dependents sought review of a judgment of the Hamilton District Court (Kansas), which found in favor of appellees, an employer and an insurer, in a workers' compensation action upholding the constitutionality of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-510b(i) in limiting workers' compensation death benefits to those who were not citizens or residents of the United States.


OVERVIEW: The employee's dependents contested the constitutionality of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-510b(i) in limiting workers' compensation death benefits to $ 750 dollars to nonresident aliens. United States residents or citizen benefits were limited to $ 200,000 dollars. The trial court concluded that the § 44-510b(i) was constitutional. On review, the court reversed and found that the dependents' right of action was derivative of and dependent upon the employee's contract of employment. It existed because of the employee-employer relationship. The statute discriminated against a class of employees based on their dependents' alienage. The benefit limitation applied only to dependents who were nonresident aliens; however, nonresident United States citizens were entitled to the same benefits as resident citizens and resident aliens. Classifications based on alienage, with respect to resident aliens, were suspect and subject to strict scrutiny. The statute was unconstitutional and violated the Equal Protection Clauses of both the Kansas and the United States Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and found in favor of the employee's dependents against the employer and insurer.

State v. Stone


No. 68,149


Supreme Court of Kansas


253 Kan. 105; 853 P.2d 662; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 100



May 28, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick District Court, Clark V. Owens II, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the jury verdict and judgment entered in the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas). He was convicted of second-degree murder under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3402 and misdemeanor theft under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3701.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a companion were seen stealing cartons of cigarettes from a store. Three clerks chased them outside, and one clerk was killed when defendant ran over her and dragged her under the van for 500 feet. He challenged the jury instruction regarding the intent requirement for a charge of second degree murder as well as the sufficiency of the evidence and certain evidentiary rulings. The court noted that the jury instruction specifically stated that the presumption of intent could be rejected but at no time did the burden of proof ever shift to defendant. The instruction was constitutionally valid. The court found there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's verdict. The State was permitted to introduce gruesome photographs of the victim to show the extent of her injuries that caused her death. The trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury that vehicular homicide was a lesser included offense when it instructed on the lesser included offense of involuntary manslaughter. Under certain narrow factual situations such as defendant's where wanton misconduct or gross negligence was a part of the charge, vehicular homicide was not a lesser included offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and the convictions.

 

149 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. KFB Ins. Co.


No. 68,452


Supreme Court of Kansas


252 Kan. 1010; 850 P.2d 773; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 67



April 16, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee District Court; Adrian J. Allen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review from orders of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which entered a jury verdict in favor of appellee insured in an action claiming underinsured benefits, and held that the Collateral Source Benefits Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-3801 et seq., was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee insured brought an action against appellant insurer claiming underinsured motorist benefits. Prior to trial, the district court ruled that the Collateral Source Benefits Act (Act), Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 60-3801 et seq., was unconstitutional, and therefore did not admit evidence of collateral source benefits at trial. A jury found in favor of plaintiff, and appellant sought review of the verdict and district court's rulings. The court affirmed the judgment of the district court, holding that the Act was unconstitutional on equal protection grounds, because it failed to pass the rational basis test. The classification of plaintiffs by the size of their demands, under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-3802, was not relevant to a legitimate state objective. In addition, the court held that § 60-3802, was not severable from the Act, and the entire Act was therefore void. Classification was not a separate and independent provision, because to eliminate the classification would have changed the entire scheme of the Act. The invalidity of § 60-3802 affected the remainder of the Act because, absent the invalid provision, the intent of the legislature would not have been carried out.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court, holding that the Collateral Source Benefits Act (Act) was unconstitutional. The classification provision of the Act did not pass the rational basis test on equal protection grounds. The provision could not be severed from the remainder of the Act without changing its scope and doing violence to the legislative intent and, therefore, the entire Act was unconstitutional and void.

State v. Phillips


No. 67,873


Supreme Court of Kansas


252 Kan. 937; 850 P.2d 877; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 68



April 16, 1993, Opinion Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Saline District Court (Kansas), which convicted him on one count of first-degree premeditated murder, contrary to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3401 (Supp. 1992), and sentenced him to life imprisonment with a 40 year minimum, under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4624 et seq. (Supp. 1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant beat a man whom he had just met at bar to death. A jury found him guilty of first-degree premeditated murder under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4625(6) (1992 Supp.) was not unconstitutionally vague and a requested instruction was not a valid ground for appeal. Dozier v. Dozier


No. 68,472


Supreme Court of Kansas


252 Kan. 1035; 850 P.2d 789; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 74



April 16, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Johnson District Court; Gerald T. Elliott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband challenged an order from the Johnson District Court (Kansas) granting summary judgment in favor of appellee ex-wife in an action by the ex-husband alleging false arrest and imprisonment. The trial court found that the ex-husband's claims of false arrest and imprisonment failed, as a matter of law, because the restraint of the ex-husband was legal.


OVERVIEW: The parties' settlement agreement on alimony was incorporated into their divorce decree. The ex-husband fell into arrears on his alimony payments and failed to make a lump sum payment required by the trial court. The ex-wife filed an accusation in contempt. The trial court issued a bench warrant when the ex-husband failed to appear before the trial court to answer a contempt citation and show cause order. The ex-husband was arrested on the bench warrant. On appeal, the court disagreed with the ex-husband that the alimony was only contractual in nature and that the ex-husband was unconstitutionally imprisoned for his failure to pay a debt. Through incorporation into the divorce decree, the alimony agreement became a judgment rather than just a contractual agreement. The court determined that contempt proceedings were a proper method to enforce alimony. The court concluded that summary judgment was properly granted to the ex-wife as she did not cause the false arrest and imprisonment of the ex-husband but only informed the trial court of the circumstances as she perceived them and left it to the trial court to take whatever action the trial court deemed proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

152 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Blue v. McBride


No. 67,778


Supreme Court of Kansas


252 Kan. 894; 850 P.2d 852; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 77



April 16, 1993, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified July 21, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Sedgwick District Court, M. Kay Royse, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a judgment of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which held that S.B. 486, 1990 Kans. Sess. Laws ch. 52, codified and amended in scattered sections of Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 8-2401 et seq., violated the United States and Kansas Constitutions, entered temporary and permanent injunctions against the enforcement of the statute, and awarded plaintiff brokers and credit unions attorney fees and costs.


OVERVIEW: Two automobile brokers and six credit unions who referred business to the brokers brought suit challenging the constitutionality of S.B. 486, 1990 Kans. Sess. Laws ch. 52, codified and amended in scattered sections of The Vehicle Dealers and Manufacturers Licensing Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 8-2401 et seq., which eliminated the business of brokering new and used automobiles. The trial court found the statute unconstitutional, issued a permanent injunction, and awarded attorney fees. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the statute did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment on either due process or equal protection grounds. The statute also did not violate the First Amendment. The purposes of the statute were an expression of legislative concerns over problems that existed or which could rationally be conceived to occur in the future in sales and distribution of automobiles unless remedial action was taken. As the statute was held to be constitutional, the decision granting the brokers and the credit unions attorney fees was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment that S.B. 486 was violative of the Fourteenth Amendment was reversed and the constitutionality of the legislative enactment eliminating the business of brokering new and used automobiles was upheld. The award of attorney fees was reversed and the permanent injunction issued was vacated.

 

153 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kingsley


No. 67,260


Supreme Court of Kansas


252 Kan. 761; 851 P.2d 370; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 69



April 16, 1993, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent civil proceeding at In re M.E.O., 1993 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 395 (Kan. Ct. App., May 7, 1993)
Post-conviction relief denied at Kingsley v. State, 2004 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 806 (Kan. Ct. App., Apr. 2, 2004)
Motion sustained by, Writ of habeas corpus denied Kingsley v. McKune, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 28555 (D. Kan., Nov. 17, 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Kingsley, 2007 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 809 (Kan. Ct. App., Feb. 23, 2007)
Motion denied by State v. Kingsley, 299 Kan. 896, 326 P.3d 1083, 2014 Kan. LEXIS 282 (June 13, 2014)
Motion denied by State v. Kingsley, 2017 Kan. LEXIS 294 (Kan., June 2, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick District Court; M. Kay Royse, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Sedgwick County District Court (Kansas) of conviction for first-degree murder, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3401(a)(Supp. 1992), aggravated robbery, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3427, aggravated arson, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3719, and forgery, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3710(b). Defendant also appealed the sentences imposed by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was alleged to have robbed and killed the victim, and then to have set fire to her home. Defendant argued on appeal, inter alia, that his conviction of aggravated arson was improper and the court erred in its instruction to the jury on that offense. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction of aggravated arson and vacated that sentence, and held that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3719, required that the act of arson had to be committed upon a building or property in which there was a human being. The court held that in the context of that statute, a human being was a living person.The evidence indicated that the victim was dead when the arson occurred. In light of the court's finding that aggravated arson required the presence of a living person, there was a failure of proof in that respect and the jury could not have concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that aggravated arson was committed where the fire occurred after the victim was dead.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions of first-degree murder, aggravated robbery, and forgery and reversed the conviction of and sentence for aggravated arson, and remanded to resentence defendant.

State v. Harkness


No. 66,809


Supreme Court of Kansas


252 Kan. 510; 847 P.2d 1191; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 47



March 5, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Johnson District Court; Gerald L. Hougland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Johnson District Court (Kansas), which convicted him for aggravated kidnapping, rape, aggravated sodomy, and aggravated assault. Defendant was committed to a State hospital, but nine years later he was returned to the trial court for sentencing pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3431.


OVERVIEW: Defendant assigned a number of errors, including a claim that he was mentally competent at the time of trial and sentencing based on his psychiatric problems. The court disagreed, noting that the trial court had ample opportunity to observe his conduct and demeanor at trial, but found him competent. Moreover, the court rejected his contention that his psychotropic medication deemed his competency invalid because it was synthetically produced. With regard to his competency at sentencing, it was proper to release him for sentencing when the hospital found that defendant no longer benefited from the treatment, even where they opined that he was dangerous. The court found that the weight and sufficiency of evidence supported the conviction, and the jury was justified to find that he was not insane under the M'Naghten test. The court determined that, although the instructions might have been worded better, they did not unconstitutionally shift the burden of proof to defendant. However, the court agreed with defendant's contention that the three counts of aggravated assault were multiplicitous with his convictions for aggravated kidnapping.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, except as to the count for aggravated assault, which was reversed. The case was remanded with directions to vacate the sentence imposed on that count.

Unified Sch. Dist. No. 380 v. McMillen


No. 68,220


Supreme Court of Kansas


252 Kan. 451; 845 P.2d 676; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 17



January 22, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Marshall District Court, J. D. Euler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenured teacher sought review of a judgment by the Marshall District Court (Kansas), which upheld a decision by appellee school district not to renew the teacher's teaching contract. The trial court held the Kan. Stat. Ann. § 72-5443 (Supp. 1991), which governed the due process afforded to a tenured teacher in a dispute regarding the nonrenewal of a teacher's contract violated Kan. Const. art. 6, §§ 2, 5.


OVERVIEW: A due process hearing was held after the teacher was advised of the district's intent not to renew his contract. The hearing committee held the district did not show good cause to not renew the teacher's contract. The district court concluded it was not bound by the committee's decision because § 72-5443 removed from the local school board the authority to make a final decision of whether a teacher's contract should be renewed and that it violated Kan. Const. art. 6, §§ 2, 5. The court reversed and remanded. The court held the district was entitled to appeal the committee's decision under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-2101(d) (Supp. 1991), and that the district was an aggrieved party under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 72-5443(b) (Supp. 1991). The court held that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 72-5443 (Supp. 1991) did not violate Kan. Const. art. 6, §§ 2, 6. The court concluded that the powers of the committee did not unconstitutionally impinge on the state board of education's general supervisory authority, and that the hiring and firing of teachers was not a duty of the state board of education. Further, the right to hire and fire teachers was a right created by statute and not the Kansas Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the district and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Walker


No. 66,225


Supreme Court of Kansas


252 Kan. 279; 845 P.2d 1; 1993 Kan. LEXIS 1



January 22, 1993, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick District Court, Keith Sanborn, Paul W. Clark, and Paul Buchanan, Judges.
State v. Walker, 252 Kan. 117, 843 P.2d 203, 1992 Kan. LEXIS 195 (Dec. 11, 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which convicted him of first-degree premeditated murder, aggravated robbery, aggravated assault, attempted aggravated criminal sodomy, aggravated criminal sodomy, battery, aggravated battery, two counts of theft and rape, three counts of aggravated burglary, and four counts of aggravated kidnapping. Defendant also challenged the imposition of a "hard 40" sentence.


OVERVIEW: Selection of prospective jurors from voter registration lists did not violate defendant's constitutional rights. His confession in an interview eight hours after he arrived at the police station was properly admitted. The delay in interviewing him did not affect its voluntariness. The heinous, atrocious, and cruel aggravating factor was not unconstitutionally vague, and its imposition was supported by evidence of the lengthy assault and slow death of the murder victim that was stomped to death. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Grissom


No. 66,268


Supreme Court of Kansas


251 Kan. 851; 840 P.2d 1142; 1992 Kan. LEXIS 180



November 10, 1992, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended November 13, 1992. Second Amendment November 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Johnson District Court; William G. Gray, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed. Sentences for four counts of robbery and one count of aggravated burglary vacated and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state indicted defendant for crimes arising out of the murder of three women. The Johnson District Court (Kansas) entered judgment convicting defendant of: three counts of first-degree murder; one count of aggravated kidnapping; four counts of robbery; two counts of aggravated burglary; and one count of misdemeanor theft. Defendant appealed the convictions and the enhanced sentences imposed by the district court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the state failed to make a prima facie showing of the corpus delicti for the homicide for each of the three murder charges. The essence of his argument was that the circumstantial evidence presented was insufficient. The court held that the corpus delicti for homicide on each of the three counts of murder was established. The court reasoned that in viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the state, it was clear the state established a pattern of behavior and that a rational factfinder could have found that defendant entered the victims' apartments with keys he had acquired, surprised them, and threatened them with a gun or knife. The court also held that: 1) jurisdiction was proper in Kansas; 2) the evidence was sufficient to sustain the murder all the convictions; 3) defendant's claims concerning the multiplicity were unfounded; 4) defendant's truck was abandoned and that therefore, defendant had no expectation of privacy in its regard; and 5) that the enhancement of defendant's sentence was improper it was not established that the underlying offense had been committed after a judgment of conviction on a prior offense.


OUTCOME: The convictions for all the offenses were affirmed, as were the four life sentences and the one-year sentence for misdemeanor theft. The remaining six sentences were vacated and remanded for resentencing.

State ex rel. Braun v. Tract of Land in the Northwest Quarter of Section Four


No. 66,641


Supreme Court of Kansas


251 Kan. 685; 840 P.2d 453; 1992 Kan. LEXIS 168



October 30, 1992, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 16 Kan. App. 2d 757, 829 P.2d 600 (1992). Appeal from Ellis District Court; Tom Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals reversing the district court is affirmed. Judgment of the district court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Kansas appealed an order of the Court of Appeals (Kansas), which reversed the judgment of the trial court subjecting a forfeiture claimant's real property to forfeiture. The claimant had entered a plea of no contest to one count of conspiracy to possess marijuana with intent to sell.


OVERVIEW: The claimant contended that the property at issue was his homestead and was protected from forfeiture by Kan. Const. Bill Rights § 12 and Kan. Const. art. 15, § 9. The state relied on Kan. Stat. Ann. § 65-4135(a)(7)(A) (Supp. 1991), which provided that the claimant of a homestead who had been convicted of a violation of the Uniform Controlled Substances Act was presumed to have consented to the forfeiture of the homestead by committing the violation. The claimant contended that the homestead exemption was a constitutional right not subject to legislative intrusion, and argued that the legislature lacked authority to limit the homestead exemption. The court concluded that the court of appeals correctly held that the forfeiture of the claimant's real property was a forced sale in violation of Kan. Const. art. 15, § 9. The court noted that Kan. Const. art. 15, § 9 specifically provided for three exceptions to the homestead exemption, and that forfeiture was not one of them. Moreover, Kansas had zealously protected the family rights in homestead property by liberally construing the homestead provision in order to safeguard its humanitarian and soundly social and economic purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals reversing the judgment of the trial court.

Supreme Court of Kansas

July 10, 1992, Opinion Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, after a jury trial, from the Johnson District Court (Kansas) for first-degree murder, his sentence to life in prison, and an order to pay restitution in the amount of $ 1,000.


OVERVIEW: The victim's wife was defendant's lover. Defendant's keys and his fingerprint were found in a search of a rental car that they returned after the victim had been shot. Affirming the conviction, the court said that there was sufficient evidence for a rational factfinder to have found defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. Ann. § 21-4603(2)(c) (Supp. 1989) by ordering both incarceration and restitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, but reversed the restitution order and remanded for technical corrections to the restitution portion of the sentence.

St. Francis Reg'l Medical Ctr. v. Bowles


No. 66,075


Supreme Court of Kansas


251 Kan. 334; 836 P.2d 1123; 1992 Kan. LEXIS 144



July 10, 1992, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 16 Kan. App. 2d 374, 823 P.2d 226 (1991). Appeal from Sedgwick District Court, William D. Rustin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirming the District Court is affirmed. Judgment of the District Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of a judgment of the court of appeals (Kansas), which affirmed the trial court's judgment that held the wife was liable to appellee medical center for her husband's medical expenses.


OVERVIEW: The medical center sued the husband and the wife for the cost of unpaid medical services provided to the husband. The husband confessed he owed money to the medical center but that he was financially unable to satisfy the delinquent balance due. The trial court ruled that the wife was liable for the husband's medical expenses. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed the appellate court's judgment and expanded the common-law doctrine of necessaries to apply to husbands and wives equally. The court held that the doctrine of necessaries in its historical form violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution because historically the doctrine was applied to husbands only. The court ruled that before a creditor could seek payment from a spouse, the creditor must first pursue collection from the person who received the necessary goods or services. The court held that only if the spouse who received the benefits had insufficient resources to satisfy the debt could the other spouse be liable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment that affirmed the trial court's judgment.

The court held that because the father failed to brief on appeal the issue of the AHO's acceptance as evidence of the mother's exhibits that had not been provided to him prior to the hearing, the issue was deemed abandoned.

State of Kansas v. Darrell Bailey


No. 66,511


Supreme Court of Kansas


251 Kan. 156; 834 P.2d 342; 1992 Kan. LEXIS 113



May 22, 1992, Opinion Filed

Related proceeding at State v. Walker, 252 Kan. 117, 843 P.2d 203, 1992 Kan. LEXIS 195 (Dec. 11, 1992)
Related proceeding at Johnson v. State, 2002 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 690 (Kan. Ct. App., July 12, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick District Court, Russell Cranmer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Sedgwick County (Kansas), convicting him of first-degree murder, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3401, rape, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3502, aggravated criminal sodomy, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3506, aggravated robbery, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3427, aggravated battery, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3414, battery, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3412, and criminal damage to property, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3720.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of a number of criminal offenses, including first-degree murder, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3401, and rape, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3502. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to discharge the jury panel on the grounds that the procedure for selecting the prospective jurors from voter registration lists violated his right to a fair and impartial jury trial. The court ruled that a challenge based on alleged discrimination in the selection of a jury necessarily required a showing that a recognizable identifiable class of persons, otherwise entitled to be jury members, was purposefully and systematically excluded from jury service. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the judgment, concluding that defendant failed to establish a prima facie case that the jury panel systematically or purposefully excluded a cognizable group such as blacks or minorities as a whole.

Stephenson v. Sugar Creek Packing


No. 67,056


Supreme Court of Kansas


250 Kan. 768; 830 P.2d 41; 1992 Kan. LEXIS 80



April 10, 1992, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Crawford District Court; Nelson E. Toburen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a decision of the Crawford District Court (Kansas), which affirmed the workers compensation award made to her by the administrative law judge in favor of appellees, the employer and the insurer.


OVERVIEW: The employee received a workers compensation award from the administrative law judge, which was affirmed by the trial court. The employee sought review and contended that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-510d(a)(23) (1991 Supp.) violated the equal protection clause because it differentiated between repetitive and single injuries. Under § 44-510d, whenever the employee was entitled to compensation for repetitive use conditions occurring in opposite upper extremities, the compensation was to be computed as separate scheduled injuries and the percentage was to be increased by 20 percent of the determined loss. The court held that, the determination of whether a right was a fundamental interest was whether the right asserted was explicitly or implicitly guaranteed by the constitution. Because the statute had not affected a fundamental right, the rational basis test was to be applied in determining equal protection rights. The court held that the statute discriminated between repetitive and single injuries and failed to pass the rational basis test. The court found that it was unconstitutional. The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded a judgment of the trial court and held that the workers compensation statute violated the equal protection clause because it failed to pass the rational basis test of the equal protection clause.

 

167 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Jarvis v. Drake


No. 66,434


Supreme Court of Kansas


250 Kan. 645; 830 P.2d 23; 1992 Kan. LEXIS 93



April 10, 1992, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wyandotte District Court; John J. Bukaty, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of a judgment from the Wyandotte District Court (Kansas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, the ex-husband of one of his clients, in his action to recover for malicious prosecution, libel, and tortious interference with contract. The ex-husband also sought review from the district court's denial of his request for attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: The ex-husband argued that at all times pertinent to the allegations made by the attorney, he was cloaked with immunity, because he had instituted a disciplinary proceeding against the attorney. Kan. Sup. Ct. R. 223 provided that complaints in the course of disciplinary proceedings were to be deemed made in the course of judicial proceedings and that all participants were entitled to judicial immunity and all rights afforded public officials. The court agreed and affirmed the judgment. The court held that judicial immunity applied even when a judge was accused of acting maliciously and corruptly, though the privilege was not for the protection or benefit of a malicious or corrupt judge, but for the benefit of the public, whose interest it was that the judges should be at liberty to exercise their functions with independence and without fear of consequences. Because rule 223 was applicable to the action, the ex-husband was protected from the attorney's action by judicial immunity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Harding v. K.C. Wall Products, Inc.


No. 66,513


Supreme Court of Kansas


250 Kan. 655; 831 P.2d 958; 1992 Kan. LEXIS 94; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,148



April 10, 1992, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick District Court, William D. Rustin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation appealed from the order of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas) that denied its motion for summary judgment in a negligence and strict liability action by plaintiff, an executor of her husband's estate, which alleged that her husband's death was caused by defendant's manufacture and sale of asbestos-containing products.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, an executor of her husband's estate, filed an action against defendant corporation, alleging negligence and strict liability following the death of her husband, a painting contractor, who had been diagnosed with malignant pleural mesothelioma. Plaintiff alleged that her husband's death was caused by exposure to asbestos-containing products manufactured and sold by defendant. Defendant alleged that plaintiff's claim was barred by the statute of limitations. The district court denied defendant's motion for summary judgment, and defendant filed an interlocutory appeal. The court affirmed and remanded the case for further proceedings, holding that the applicable statute of limitations was the statute in effect at the time the action was filed, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-3303 (1991), which provided a limitation for actions that arose out of a latent disease caused by asbestos. The retroactive provision of § 60-3303(e), which revived actions prohibited by the two-year statute of limitations for tort actions, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-513 (1991), did not violate the state constitution or U.S. Const. amend. XIV because defendant had no vested right in a statute of limitations defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and remanded the district court's order which denied defendant corporation's motion for summary judgment in a negligence and strict liability action by plaintiff, an executor of her husband's estate, which alleged that her husband's death was caused by defendant's products because the applicable statute of limitations, which revived actions prohibited by a prior limitations statute, was not unconstitutional.

State v. Simms


No. 65,754


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


1992 Kan. LEXIS 54



February 28, 1992, Filed
