PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Lyon district court; WILLIAM J. DICK, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Lyon District Court (Kansas), which convicted and sentenced defendant for kidnapping in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3420, aggravated robbery in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3427, and attempted robbery in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3301 (Supp. 1991) and Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3427.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted and sentenced defendant for kidnapping, aggravated robbery, and attempted robbery. Defendant failed to demonstrate prejudice and failed to provide sufficient information in his brief for the court to undertake an independent assessment of possible prejudice.

OVERVIEW: Attorneys sought to recover money damages for legal services rendered under the court-appointed system prior to July 1, 1988. PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purported class of taxpayers challenged an order of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which dismissed their mandamus action against defendants, the Kansas Department of Revenue and the Johnson County Board of Commissioners, that challenged the constitutionality of Kan. Admin. Reg. 92-51-21.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers brought a class action that alleged that the alphabetical staggered registration system for motor vehicle registration and taxation that was established by Kan. Admin. Reg. 92-51-21 unconstitutionally discriminated against persons whose registration month was any month after February. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal order.

Dean v. State


No. 66,374


Supreme Court of Kansas


250 Kan. 417; 826 P.2d 1372; 1992 Kan. LEXIS 63



February 28, 1992, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Johnson District Court; Larry McClain, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of the judgment of the Johnson District Court (Kansas), which dismissed their civil actions against appellees, a state, a Department of Revenue, a Secretary of Revenue, a Director of Property Valuation, and county treasurers, for lack of subject matter jurisdiction based upon the taxpayers' failure to exhaust administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers argued that appellees used the county average tax from two years prior rather than one year prior to calculate motor vehicle taxes. Because of this, the motor vehicle tax was higher than it would have been had the prior year's county average tax been used. The taxpayers filed suit to recover the excess motor vehicle tax they paid. The district court dismissed their suit for lack of subject matter jurisdiction based upon the taxpayers' failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The taxpayers appealed and the court affirmed. The court found that the taxpayers' claim for recovery of the motor vehicle registration tax was an attempt to seek tax relief without first complying with Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-2005 (1991). Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 79-2005 (1991), and 74-2426 (1991) provided the taxpayers with a clear and certain remedy for complete and adequate relief and, therefore, had to be complied with before resorting to the courts. The district court properly dismissed the taxpayers' claims for the recovery of taxes for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

173 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Hainline v. Bond


No. 66,337


Supreme Court of Kansas


250 Kan. 217; 824 P.2d 959; 1992 Kan. LEXIS 18



January 17, 1992, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee District Court, Fred S. Jackson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teacher sought review of the decision of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which affirmed the suspension of his teaching certificate that was imposed by appellee, Kansas State Board of Education, upon the complaint of appellee, secretary to the professional practices commission.


OVERVIEW: After the teacher was arrested for burglary and theft, the commission filed a complaint seeking revocation of his teaching certificate. Thereafter, the Board suspended the teacher's certificate. The district court affirmed the Board's order. The court held that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 72-1383 was not in derogation of Kan. Const. art. 6, § 2 because it neither reduced the Board's supervisory authority by delegating any part thereof to another entity nor did it require the Board to do or not do anything. Further, to hold that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 72-1383 conflicted with Kan. Admin. Regs. 91-1-61 would improperly repeal Kan. Stat. Ann. § 72-1383 by implication. Moreover, the teaching profession had justification for the discipline of a person within it ranks who committed a felony, and there was a least a presumption that the teacher's felonious conduct had a sufficient nexus to fitness to teach to warrant the action by the Board. Additionally, there was no right to privacy involved in the commission of a burglary. Finally, adequate notice, that felonious conduct was prohibited and within the meaning of the § 72-1383 term "immorality," was present and defeated any claim of vagueness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision.

State v. Yura


No. 66,273


Supreme Court of Kansas


250 Kan. 198; 825 P.2d 523; 1992 Kan. LEXIS 21



January 17, 1992, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sumner District Court; Lloyd K. McDaniel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Kansas, challenged an order of the Sumner District Court (Kansas) entered in a probation revocation, which dismissed the State's motion to revoke appellee's probation on the ground that the basis for the revocation petition was based upon unresolved criminal charges. The district court also refused to admit laboratory test results under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3716(2) (Supp. 1990) and an affidavit of the lab technician.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was on probation for possession of marijuana. As a condition of her probation, she had to obey the law and not possess, use, or traffic in controlled substances. She was required to submit to blood/urine tests upon request of the court services officer. While on probation, she was arrested for serving alcohol to minors. A urine test was ordered, which showed the presence of marijuana. The State filed a petition to revoke her probation based upon the arrest and the lab results. The trial court dismissed the petition, holding that the revocation proceeding was premature because the criminal charges were unresolved. It also held that the lab results and the technician's affidavit were inadmissible because they were hearsay. The court held that the revocation petition was proper, even though the criminal charges were unresolved, because the standard of proof in the revocation proceeding was lower than that of a criminal prosecution. The lab results and affidavit were admissible under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3716(2) (Supp. 1990), which authorized the admission of affidavits constituting relevant written statements made under oath stating the results of a laboratory test.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the revocation petition and denying the admission of the lab results and the technician's affidavit, and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

State v. Chisholm


No. 66,123


Supreme Court of Kansas


250 Kan. 153; 825 P.2d 147; 1992 Kan. LEXIS 26



January 17, 1992, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Riley District Court; Harlan W. Graham, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed findings of the Riley District Court (Kansas) that requiring a child witness to testify in open court in defendant's presence would prevent her from reasonably communicating to a jury and effectively rendered the child unavailable to testify under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3434 and therefore a closed-circuit procedure was proper. The court had remanded his conviction of aggravated incest, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3603.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had put the burden on the State to prove that the closed circuit procedure was necessary. The State showed a video tape of the child answering questions when defendant was not present and contrasted an appearance of apprehension when he was present. The court affirmed the conviction, but the United States Supreme Court vacated and remanded it. The court remanded the case to the trial court, which held a non-evidentiary hearing. The trial judge relied on his own impressions and observations of the child. There was no evidence or testimony by any psychologist or mental health expert. The court ruled that although there was no specific evidentiary hearing, review of the record reflected all the procedural safeguards to ensure defendant's constitutional right of confrontation were present. The court explained that the legislature determined that the closed circuit procedure was appropriate for any child under 13 years old but, in accordance with the Court's interpretation of the Sixth Amendment, an individualized finding of clear and convincing evidence that testifying in defendant's presence would traumatize the child so that she was unable to communicate was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

 

176 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Guillan v. Watts


No. 64,874


Supreme Court of Kansas


249 Kan. 606; 822 P.2d 582; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 211



December 6, 1991, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 15 Kan. App. 2d 405, 808 P.2d 889 (1991). Appeal from Shawnee District Court; Fred S. Jackson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirming in part and reversing in part the decision of the district court is affirmed as modified. Judgment of the district court is affirmed in part and reversed in part and the case is remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insured challenged an order of the Court of Appeals (Kansas) finding that appellee insurer was properly allowed to intervene in the insured's action against an underinsured motorist, that the insurer was not bound by the underinsured motorist's confession of judgment, and reversible error was committed by the trial court's failure to instruct the jury that it was unlawful to drive faster than 35 mph at the location of the collision.


OVERVIEW: The insured notified his insurer that the other driver was underinsured and that the driver offered to settle her liability for her policy limits. The insurer intervened but did not substitute payment within 60 days and waived its subrogation rights against the underinsured driver. The trial court found each party 50 percent at fault and awarded no damages. The appellate court reversed in part and affirmed in part. On appeal, the court affirmed the appellate court as modified. The insurer was not bound by the agreement between the insured and the underinsured driver. There must be a trial to apportion the fault between the two drivers to determine if the insured's damages exceeded the limits of the underinsured's automobile liability insurance limits. Once notified of an action, if the insurer elected not to intervene, the insurer was bound by a judgment obtained in the action. The trial court did err in refusing to instruct the jury that it was unlawful to drive faster than 35 mph at the site of the collision because there was sufficient evidence to support the insured's negligence per se argument and the instructions given did not adequately cover the theory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision as modified and remanded the case for a new trial. A judicial determination of fault between the parties was not required to bind the insurer when a settlement agreement was entered and the insurer elected not to intervene.

 

177 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Kan. v. Risjord


Nos. 65,818, 65,819


Supreme Court of Kansas


249 Kan. 497; 819 P.2d 638; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 163



October 25, 1991, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 29, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Johnson District Court, Gerald L. Hougland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Kansas sought review of the judgment of the Johnson District Court (Kansas) finding that Johnson County, Kansas, Park and Recreation District Board Rules and Regulations, art. 1, § 6, under which appellee horseback riders were charged with riding horses in a park without a valid permit, was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and the Kansas Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The regulation provided that horses were to be ridden only in designated areas in the park and not on paved roadways or trails except for designated crossings and that each horse being ridden in the park was to display a valid horseback riding permit. The horseback riders contended that the regulation curtailed their fundamental right to travel and violated their equal protection and due process rights. On review, the court found that, under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 19-2868(g), the Board had authority to adopt, promulgate, and enforce reasonable rules and regulations for the operation of parks. Preventing accidents and reducing the seriousness of accidents on public roadways was a legitimate governmental interest and limiting traffic on public roadways to exclude animal traffic was a valid exercise of the Board's police power. Moreover, all equestrians were treated alike, and the distinct characteristics of horses presented a justifiable reason for creating a separate regulation based upon health and safety concerns. Thus, applying the rational basis test, the Board's regulation was reasonably related to the government's legitimate objective and was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

178 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Sharples v. Roberts


No. 65,664


Supreme Court of Kansas


249 Kan. 286; 816 P.2d 390; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 152



August 7, 1991, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee District Court, Fred S. Jackson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient filed a medical malpractice action. The Shawnee District Court (Kansas) granted separate orders of summary judgment to defendants, referring physician, treating physician, and medical group. The patient appealed. The case was transferred from the Court of Appeals pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 20-3018(c).


OVERVIEW: The patient alleged that the physicians' negligence had resulted in the loss of a kidney. The treating physician had died, so the patient sued the medical group. The trial court granted defendants' motions for summary judgment. The court affirmed. The patient's remedy was to have brought the action against the treating physician's estate, as provided by the probate code, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 59-2238, 59-2239 (1990 Supp.), and the Health Care Provider Insurance Availability Act, not against his employer, the medical group. Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3403(h) barred the claim against the medical group. The expert testimony was insufficient to establish that the delay in testing or referral had probably caused or contributed to the victim's deterioration in physical condition or the loss of his kidney. The testimony fell far short of the degree of medical probability or certainty required to support the necessary element of causation. Without expert testimony that the alleged negligence of the physicians had been the proximate cause of the patient's injury, the trial court was correct in granting summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Barker v. State


No. 65,848


Supreme Court of Kansas


249 Kan. 186; 815 P.2d 46; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 136; 14 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1089



July 12, 1991, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] REPORTER'S NOTE: Case No. 65,848 was reversed by the United States Supreme Court in an opinion filed April 21, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Shawnee District Court; Adrian J. Allen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers, who were all retirees of the military, challenged a judgment of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant State of Kansas in the taxpayers' § 1983 class action. The trial court found that the Kansas Income Tax Act (KITA), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-3201 et seq., as applied to military retirement pay, was constitutional and did not violate 4 U.S.C.S. § 111.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after the United States Supreme Court held that a Michigan statute imposing a state income tax on retirement benefits of federal civil service retirees, while exempting retirement benefits of State retirees, violated the doctrine of intergovernmental tax immunity, the subject class action suits were filed, challenging KITA. KITA taxed federal military retirement benefits, but exempted retirement benefits received by State and local government retirees. The taxpayers claimed that KITA discriminated against federal military retirees and, therefore, violated 4 U.S.C.S. § 111 (1988), intergovernmental tax immunity, the privileges and immunities clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Kan. Const. art. 11, § 2. The taxpayers all paid Kansas income taxes on federal military retirement pay. The court held that military retirement pay was reduced current compensation for reduced current services and that KITA was constitutional under principles of intergovernmental tax immunity and under Kan. Const. art II, § 2. The court further held that the discriminatory tax bore a reasonable relationship to the subject taxed and that the tax was not arbitrary or capricious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

180 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reed


No. 65,152


Supreme Court of Kansas


248 Kan. 792; 811 P.2d 1163; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 98



May 24, 1991, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee District Court; William Randolph Carpenter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a ruling of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas) that held that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4603(3)(a) (Supp. 1989), which provides that a district court shall modify a defendant's sentence when recommended by the State Reception and Diagnostic Center unless specific findings are made by the district court, was unconstitutional on separation of power grounds.


OVERVIEW: After the State Reception and Diagnostic Center (SRDC) recommended a modification of defendant's sentence for an aggravated sexual battery conviction, defendant moved for modification of his sentence under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4603 (Supp. 1989). The district court denied the motion, ruling that § 21-4603 was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers doctrine. Defendant appealed. In reversing and remanding for reconsideration of defendant's motion, the court concluded that § 21-4603 was constitutional and did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. The statute did not unnecessarily or unconstitutionally restrict the discretionary power of a district court, which had the discretion to reject an SRDC recommendation for modification when both the safety of the public would be jeopardized and the welfare of defendant would not be served by the modification. The SRDC merely made recommendations; the final determination rested with the district court, which was to consider not only the SRDC recommendation but other sentencing factors as well.


OUTCOME: The ruling of the district court was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the district court with directions to reconsider defendant's motion to modify his sentence.

 

181 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Bair v. Peck


No. 65,240


Supreme Court of Kansas


248 Kan. 824; 811 P.2d 1176; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 100



May 24, 1991, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification of a question of law from the United States District Court for the District of Kansas, Sam A. Crow, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The question certified is determined.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an underlying medical malpractice case, the United States District Court for the District of Kansas submitted a certified question of whether Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3403(h) violated Kan. Const. B. of R. §§ 1, 5, 18, for defendant medical associations sought judgment on the pleadings under § 40-3403(h).


OVERVIEW: Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3403(h), part of the Health Care Provider Insurance Availability Act (Act), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3401, et seq., abolished vicarious liability for health care providers. Two defendant medical associations sought judgment on the pleadings under the statute and the United States District Court for the District of Kansas certified the question of whether Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3403(h) violated Kan. Const. B. of R. §§ 1, 5, 18. Having determined the rational basis test applied, the court held the statute did not violate principles of equal protection under Kan. Const. § 1 because it was rationally related to the legislature's goal of decreasing the cost of malpractice insurance. The statute did not violate Kan. Const. B. of R. § 5 because the right to trial by jury had nothing to do with the collection of damages. The statute did not violate Kan. Const. B. of R. § 18 because, while it abolished a remedy at common law, the Act to which it was an amendment provided a quid pro quo in the form of mandatory malpractice insurance. The court found no constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that the statute that abolished vicarious liability for health care providers did not violate the state constitution.

State v. Berberich


No. 65,306


Supreme Court of Kansas


248 Kan. 854; 811 P.2d 1192; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 104



May 24, 1991, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee District Court; James P. Buchele, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which convicted him of possession of: (1) methamphetamine, contrary to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 65-4127b(a)(2) (Supp. 1988); (2) drug paraphernalia, contrary to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 65-4152; marijuana, contrary to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 65-4127b(a)(3) (Supp. 1988); and (4) methamphetamine, without affixing the official Kansas drug tax stamp, contrary to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-5208.


OVERVIEW: While executing a search warrant, an officer saw defendant arrive with a duffel bag. He was intercepted and searched. A paper sack and a duffel bag contained drug paraphernalia, marijuana, and methamphetamine. Drug tax stamps were not affixed to either substance. Defendant admitted possession for his own use. The trial court denied a pretrial motion to dismiss the charge of possession of methamphetamine with intent to sell as an included offense of violating the Kansas Drug Tax Act (Act). Also denied was a posttrial motion to set aside the latter conviction on grounds that the Act violated the Due Process Clause by imposing an unconstitutional penalty. On appeal, the court held that possession of a controlled substance was distinct from the offense of possession without affixing drug tax stamps, and neither was an included offense of the other. The court affirmed the holding that the Act did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment right to due process by virtue of its dual purpose of generating tax revenue and discouraging drug possession and distribution. Further, relying on U.S. Supreme Court cases, the court held that defendant's due process rights were not violated by the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for possession of methamphetamine, possession of drug paraphernalia, possession of marijuana, and possession of methamphetamine without affixing the official Kansas drug tax stamp.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Shawnee District Court (Kansas) for first-degree murder based upon a killing committed in the perpetration of the abuse of a child in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3401(c) (1989 Supp.).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of killing his girlfriend's three-moth old son. Vakas v. Kansas Bd. of Healing Arts


No. 65,552


Supreme Court of Kansas


248 Kan. 589; 808 P.2d 1355; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 66



April 12, 1991, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick District Court; Thomas C. Raum, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor sought review of an order Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which upheld a decision by appellee, the Kansas Board of Healing Art, which, acting under the authority of the Healing Arts Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 65-2801 et seq., revoked the doctor's license to practice medicine and surgery and denied the doctor's application for the reinstatement of his license.


OVERVIEW: The Board administered the Healing Arts Act (Act), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 65-2801 et seq. The doctor held a license from the Board to practice medicine and surgery. Years later, the Board revoked the doctor's license as a result of alleged professional incompetence and unprofessional conduct. The Board rejected the doctor's application for reinstatement of his license, and the Board declined to reconsider its decision. The doctor petitioned for judicial review in the district court pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 77-621(c). The district court upheld the Board's decision. Upon review, the court affirmed the judgment. Although the legislature did not promulgate specific guidelines for the Board to follow when making a decision on a petition for reinstatement, the court held that the Act anticipated that the Board would consider the grounds for revoking the license as well as the stated purpose of the Act. Thus, the court determined that the Board considered all of the evidence and, after doing so, concluded that reinstatement was inappropriate; therefore, the Board did not act arbitrarily or capriciously when it refused to reinstate the doctor's license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

187 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Kennon v. State


No. 64,373


Supreme Court of Kansas


248 Kan. 515; 809 P.2d 546; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 71



April 12, 1991, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in an unpublished decision filed September 28, 1990. Appeal from Sedgwick District Court, Karen M. Humphreys, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirming the district court is reversed. Judgment of the district court is reversed and the case is remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kansas), which affirmed a trial court order denying petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus and permitted petitioner's extradition to Alabama. Petitioner contended that the trial court erred in denying his application because the facts did not prove he was a fugitive from justice under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-2702 and that the denial of his petition deprived him of due process.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought review of the appellate court's decision affirming the trial court's order denying petitioner's writ application. He had been arrested in Kansas based on criminal charges in Alabama and sought a writ to preclude his extradition to Alabama under the Kansas Uniform Criminal Extradition Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-2701 et seq., after his extradition to Alabama was demanded by the Alabama governor. Petitioner asserted that it had not been established that he was a fugitive from justice as required by Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-2702 and that the extradition documents were framed under an alternative statute, thereby denying petitioner the gubernatorial discretion which was his due process right under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-2706. The court on appeal reversed the judgments of both the appellate and trial courts based on its determination that petitioner's extradition erroneously proceeded under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-2702, requiring mandatory extradition, instead of § 22-2706. Because the extradition documents did not accurately set forth that petitioner's Kansas acts resulted in Alabama crimes, the governor was not able to exercise discretion about granting extradition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate and trial court judgments and remanded the matter to the trial court with directions to grant a writ of habeas corpus to petitioner.

 

188 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Riverside Hosp., Inc. v. State Dep't of Social & Rehabilitation Services


No. 65,670


Supreme Court of Kansas


248 Kan. 609; 808 P.2d 1348; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 63



April 12, 1991, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee District Court, Fred S. Jackson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State Department of Social and Rehabilitation Services (Kansas) sought review of a judgment from Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which ruled in favor of appellee hospital in the Department's action to recoup overpayment for Medicaid claims.


OVERVIEW: The Department determined that it had overpaid certain Medicaid claims for reimbursement submitted by the hospital and ordered recoupment. The district court affirmed in part and reversed in part the Department's action. On appeal, the court considered whether a bulletin was sufficient notice to the hospital that a major policy change had occurred, requiring the hospital to have in its files--prior to dispensing services in non-emergency situations to Medicaid patients--a written form from the patient's primary care physician. The court additionally considered whether of the use of a sample to project an error rate on all claims for reimbursement made in the period was proper. The court held that the bulletin was inadequate notice and the Department's recoupment based thereon constituted arbitrary and capricious action. The court held that no issue relative to the propriety of extrapolation from a sample, in general, or the particular extrapolation techniques utilized by the Department, were before the district court. Therefore the determination that the Department's actions were not supported by the evidence and violated the hospital's fundamental due process rights was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the judgment of the district court, holding that the Department's notice of a change in policy to the hospital was inadequate. The court reversed in part the district court's judgment that the Department's actions were not supported by the evidence and remanded the case to determine the proper amount of recoupment.

 

189 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Peck v. University Residence Committee


No. 65,479


Supreme Court of Kansas


248 Kan. 450; 807 P.2d 652; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 34



March 1, 1991, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 4, 1991. As Corrected March 21, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Riley District Court; Paul E. Miller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant student challenged the judgment of the Riley District Court (Kansas), which ruled that appellee state university's action in denying resident status to the student was not supported by substantial evidence and that the regulation, Kan. Admin. Regs. 88-3-2, was valid and constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The student sought review of the decision of the university residence committee, which found that the student did not qualify as a resident for fee purposes. The student contended that the residency regulation adopted by the university Board of Regents, Kan. Admin. Regs. 88-3-2, was invalid and unconstitutional. The district court did not agree. The student moved to Kansas just before attending the university and listed his maternal grandfather's home as his permanent address. He presented evidence that this was his permanent domicile. Kan. Stat. Ann. § 76-729(c)(4) and Kan. Admin. Regs. 88-3-2(a) required a physical residence in Kansas coupled with the intent to make Kansas a permanent home following the completion of education. The court found that the university residence committee's decision was supported by substantial evidence. The student did not qualify as a resident of Kansas for fee purposes. The student, however, did not sustain his burden of showing that the regulation was invalid. The state had a legitimate interest in protecting the quality of its universities and had the right to allow bona fide residents to attend on a preferential tuition basis.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's holding that the residence committee's decision was not based on substantial evidence. The court otherwise affirmed that the regulation was valid and constitutional.

 

190 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jamison


No. 64,439


Supreme Court of Kansas


248 Kan. 302; 806 P.2d 972; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 52



March 1, 1991, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick District Court, Karl W. Friedel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Kansas filed a direct appeal pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3602(b)(1) from an order of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which dismissed an information and complaint filed against defendant on the grounds that his constitutional and statutory rights to a speedy trial had been violated. Defendant was charged with driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs, and three other traffic infractions.


OVERVIEW: On April 1, 1987, defendant was arrested and issued an unverified traffic citation. On April 2, defendant pled not guilty. A hearing was set but was continued at the court's request until August 12. On that date, based on an intervening court of appeals decision holding that an unverified complaint defeated jurisdiction, the State voluntarily dismissed. It refiled a verified complaint 10 months later charging the same offenses. Defendant was arrested on August 18, 1989 and arraigned on August 21, 1989. Before trial, the trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss on speedy trial grounds. The court reversed, finding that the State's dismissal was necessary at the time given the status of the court of appeals opinion. Further, the State did not attempt to manipulate the speedy trial requirements. Thus the computation of time under the speedy trial statute did not commence until defendant's second arraignment. Between that date and the dismissal, 53 days passed, of which 36 were chargeable to defendant. Clearly, the speedy trial period had not expired when the district court dismissed. Considering all factors, the court also found no constitutional speedy trial violation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court dismissing the information and complaint filed against defendant and remanded for further proceedings.

 

191 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Stephan v. Johnson


No. 64,309


Supreme Court of Kansas


248 Kan. 286; 807 P.2d 664; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 54



March 1, 1991, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 14 Kan. App. 2d 542, 795 P.2d 411 (1990). Appeal from Shawnee District Court; James P. Buchele, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent state employee sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kansas), which affirmed a trial court order granting summary judgment to petitioner State of Kansas in the State's quo warranto action seeking the employee's removal from the Kansas State Board of Education.


OVERVIEW: The employee was elected to fill a vacancy on the Board. The State filed a quo warranto action seeking the employee's removal, arguing that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 25-1904 prohibited state employees from serving as Board members. The employee argued that § 25-1904 was unconstitutional. The district court order granting the State's motion for summary judgment was affirmed by the appellate court. The employee sought review. Upon consideration, the court dismissed the appeal. The court found that the employee's resignation from the Board had rendered the issues moot. The court noted that it was the duty of the courts to decide actual controversies by judgments that were enforceable, and not to give opinions upon moot questions and abstract propositions, or to declare principles that could not have been affected by the matter in issue before them.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the employee's appeal.

 

192 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCanon


No. 64,885


Supreme Court of Kansas


804 P.2d 1008; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 5



January 18, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Johnson district court, William G. Gray, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Johnson District Court (Kansas) which revoked his assignment to residential community corrections and imposed the original sentences of one to five years based on his convictions for attempted arson and burglary.


OVERVIEW: After defendant pled guilty to attempted arson and burglary, he was sentenced to a term of one to five years, to be served consecutively. However, the judge then assigned him to residential community corrections subject to a number of conditions. Subsequently, the State filed a motion to revoke, citing a number of community corrections violations. The motion was granted and defendant was ordered to serve the original sentence. Defendant then filed a motion to modify his sentence based on a State Reception and Diagnostic Center report pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4603(3)(a). The trial court denied the motion, finding that the statute was not applicable to the revocations of assignments to community corrections; that the statute was unconstitutional; and because the diagnostic report did not recommend probation. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court first noted that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4603(3) was not applicable to defendant's case because it became effective after he was sentenced and did not operate retrospectively. The court found that defendant was entitled to credit for jail time he spent in the residential community corrections program.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

193 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crawford


No. 63,855


Supreme Court of Kansas


248 Kan. 42; 804 P.2d 1385; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 10



January 18, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended February 4, 1991. Withdrawn October 15, 1991; Modified Opinion Reported at 1991 Kan. LEXIS 188. Rehearing Denied October 15, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in an unpublished decision filed July 6, 1990. Appeal from Sedgwick district court; DAVID W. KENNEDY, judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirming in part, reversing in part, and remanding with directions is affirmed in part and reversed in part. Judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Kansas), which affirmed in part and reversed in part her conviction of two counts of making a forged instrument in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3710(1)(a) and two counts of issuing a forged instrument in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3710(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of making and issuing forged checks while she was employed to provide live-in care for an invalid. On review, the appellate court affirmed the convictions for making forged checks but reversed as to the issuing forged check counts. Defendant sought further review on the grounds that the information failed to allege every essential element of the crimes charged and that the restitution order did not take into account her ability to pay. The court held that: (1) pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3201(2), a plain and concise written statement in the information of the essential facts was sufficient if written in the language of the statute; (2) all that was required was that the information follow the language of the statute substantially or charge the offense in equivalent words; (3) pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-4513, the trial court was required to take into account defendant's financial resources and the nature of the burden payment would impose when it determined the amount and method of payment of reimbursement; and (4) defendant's argument on her ability to pay was premature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the appellate court's judgment that had affirmed defendant's conviction for making forged checks. The court reversed the portion of the appellate court's judgment that had reversed defendant's conviction for issuing forged checks. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause with directions.

 

194 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Guardian Title Co. v. Bell


No. 64,936


Supreme Court of Kansas


248 Kan. 146; 805 P.2d 33; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 11



January 18, 1991, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 23, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Shawnee District Court; Fred S. Jackson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commissioner of Insurance of the State of Kansas sought review of a judgment from the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which held that Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 40-2404b(14)(f), (g) (Supp. 1989) were unconstitutional, and enjoined the Commissioner from enforcing them in appellee title companies' suit for declaratory and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: In the title companies' suit for declaratory and injunctive relief, the trial court held that Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 40-2404b(14)(f), (g) (Supp. 1989) were unconstitutional, and enjoined the Commissioner from enforcing them. Upon review the court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the subsections in question indicated a legislative intent to limit business that had been referred to a title insurer or title agent by a producer of title business who also had a financial interest in the title insurer or agency receiving the referral. The court held that thus, the trial court erred in holding Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-2404b(14)(f) (Supp. 1989) unconstitutionally vague. The court held that § 40-2404b(14)(f) gave sufficient standards to govern the rulemaking power of the Commissioner; thus, the legislature did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. The court held that there was a rational basis for the classification contained in § 40-2404b(14)(f), thus the exception for less populated counties did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

195 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Armored Servs. v. Wichita


No. 64,798


Supreme Court of Kansas


248 Kan. 136; 804 P.2d 987; 1991 Kan. LEXIS 18; 17 A.L.R.5th 1065



January 18, 1991, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick District Court; D. Keith Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action initiated by appellee system users against appellant city challenging a false alarm ordinance, the city sought review of the judgment of the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas) that struck down the ordinance as unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city had enacted an ordinance that provided for the assessment of penalties upon the triggering of a false alarm. The system users had businesses located in the city that were protected by burglar alarm systems. The city assessed administrative penalties against them based upon several false alarms. After exhausting their administrative remedies, the system users challenged the penalties in the trial court. The trial court ruled that there was no evidence to support the assessment of penalties, and it struck down the ordinance as unconstitutionally vague. In reversing in part, the court held that the ordinance was not vague because, by its terms, a system user was liable for a false alarm only if the central station that monitored the alarm could show fault on the part of the system user as opposed to a mechanical failure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment insofar as it held the ordinance unconstitutional, and it affirmed the judgment insofar as it relieved the system users of administrative penalties.

 

196 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Unified School Dist. No. 279 v. Secretary of Kansas Dep't of Human Resources


No. 63,805


Supreme Court of Kansas


247 Kan. 519; 802 P.2d 516; 1990 Kan. LEXIS 187; 136 L.R.R.M. 2448



December 7, 1990, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 14 Kan. App. 2d 248, 788 P.2d 867 (1990). Appeal from Jewell District Court, Richard W. Wahl, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirming in part and reversing in part the district court is affirmed in part and reversed in part. Judgment of the District Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Education challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Kansas), which affirmed in part and reversed in part the district court's decision in the Board's dispute with appellee education association regarding the interpretation of the Professional Negotiations Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 72-5413 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The association filed a complaint against the Board alleging that the unilateral contract altered certain terms that were not noticed for negotiation and that the Board's failure to negotiate terms that were not noticed was a prohibited practice. The association also alleged that the Board's refusal to make the compensation retroactive constituted bad faith. The court held that the Professional Negotiations Act did not limit the time in which to file a prohibited practice complaint to the period of negotiations. Since negotiations were completed when the unilateral contracts were issued, the Board did not coerce or interfere with the negotiations. The court found that the Board had committed a prohibited practice under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 72-5430(b)(1) by reducing the professional employees' salaries by the amount of the Board's mediation and factfinding costs. Even though negotiations had ceased prior to issuance of the Board's unilateral contract offer, charging teachers with the Board's attorney fees and other expenses created a chilling effect upon future negotiations. The Secretary had the authority to award the association money as a remedy for the prohibited practice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the decision of the appellate court and affirmed the decision of the district court.

 

197 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rupert


No. 63,753


Supreme Court of Kansas


247 Kan. 512; 802 P.2d 511; 1990 Kan. LEXIS 208



December 7, 1990, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 14 Kan. App. 2d 229, 787 P.2d 300 (1990). Appeal from Saline District Court, Gene B. Penland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals reversing the district court is reversed. Judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Kansas) reversing defendant's conviction for criminal nonsupport of a child, a violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3605(1) (Supp. 1989), after finding constitutional infirmity in the standard of proof required under § 21-3605(1)(f).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal nonsupport of a child. The appellate court reversed. On further appeal, the court reversed the appellate court's judgment and affirmed the trial court's conviction. There was a constitutional requirement that every essential element of a criminal charge must be proven beyond a reasonable doubt. Thus, the provision of § 21-3605(1)(f) provided that parentage need only be proven by a preponderance of the evidence was unconstitutional; however, the court found that striking the sentence regarding evidence required to prove parentage from § 21-3605(1)(f) did not invalidate the remainder of the statute. The court found that the constitutional error was harmless. Comments made by the prosecutor regarding defendant's failure to testify constituted harmless error.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals, reversing the district court, was reversed. The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

198 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Joe Self Chevrolet, Inc. v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 64,508


Supreme Court of Kansas


247 Kan. 625; 802 P.2d 1231; 1990 Kan. LEXIS 189



December 7, 1990, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick District Court; Montie R. Deer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of County Commissioners sought review of a decision from the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas), which granted judgment for appellee automobile dealer on the dealer's action claiming that the county's use of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-2111 in repossessing an automobile from a taxpayer was contrary to legislative intent or, in the alternative, that the statute was unconstitutional because it denied due process.


OVERVIEW: A dealer filed a declaratory judgment action claiming the county's procedure under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-2111 was contrary to legislative intent and that the statute was unconstitutional because it denied due process. The dealer claimed a security interest in a truck sold to a taxpayer and contended that the county's seizure of the truck without notice deprived him of his perfected security interest. The court affirmed the district court's judgment for the dealer and concluded that the dealer, a secured creditor, had standing and sufficient interest in the justiciable controversy to obtain a resolution as to the constitutionality of § 79-2111. The court held that the county denied the dealer due process of law and ruled that the dealer was entitled to notice of the county's intent to sell the truck to collect the taxpayer's delinquent personal property taxes. The court modified the judgment and ruled that the district court erred in declaring § 79-2111 unconstitutional since the county only applied the statute in an unconstitutional manner and the statute properly gave the tax lien upon the taxpayer's personal property a preference over any other lien existing against the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment for the automobile dealer on his action claiming that the county's use of a statute in repossessing an automobile from a taxpayer was contrary to legislative intent. The court modified the district court's judgment and ruled that the district court's had erred in declaring the statute unconstitutional.

 

199 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Leavenworth-Jefferson Electric Coop., Inc. v. Kansas Corp. Com.


No. 64,673


Supreme Court of Kansas


247 Kan. 268; 797 P.2d 874; 1990 Kan. LEXIS 157



August 30, 1990, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee District Court; Thomas W. Regan and Matthew J. Dowd, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a rural electric cooperative, challenged a judgment of the Shawnee County District Court (Kansas), which upheld the constitutionality of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 66-1,176 (Supp. 1989), a section of the Retail Electric Suppliers Act (RESA), Kan. Stat. Ann. § 66-1,170 et seq.


OVERVIEW: A city voted to allow appellee utility company to serve newly annexed territory under the utility company's existing franchise instead of granting a franchise to the rural electric cooperative. About six months later, the utility company and the electric cooperative executed an agreement for compensation to be paid to the electric cooperative pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 66-1,176 (Supp. 1989) of RESA. The electric cooperative later challenged the constitutionality of § 66-1,176 before appellee Kansas Corporation Commission and the district court. The court did not reach the merits of the electric cooperative's appeal, because it held that the electric cooperative lacked standing to challenge the statute's constitutionality. Because the electric cooperative had benefitted from the statute by obtaining compensation from the other utility company, the electric cooperative was estopped from challenging the statute's constitutionality. The court declined to issue an advisory opinion and dismissed the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

 

200 of 1377 DOCUMENTS


Parker v. State


No. 64,612


Supreme Court of Kansas


247 Kan. 214; 795 P.2d 68; 1990 Kan. LEXIS 143



July 13, 1990, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action in habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an action in habeas corpus seeking release from confinement and the State filed a motion for dismissal on the basis of mootness.


OVERVIEW: While on parole, petitioner was charged with the commission of two felonies. He was released on bond, but on the same day, petitioner's parole officer issued an arrest and detain order. Petitioner was arrested. He was convicted of felony criminal damage to property and misdemeanor battery and incarcerated for a term of one to two years. Petitioner was granted probation but remained incarcerated under the arrest and detain order. Based upon the felony conviction, petitioner's parole officer issued a second arrest and detain order charging him with parole violations. Finally, the parole board revoked petitioner's parole. Petitioner filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus seeking release from confinement. Subsequent to filing the petition, petitioner was reparoled and released from confinement, whereupon the State filed a motion for dismissal on the basis of mootness. The court denied the writ and held that petitioner was held in custody without a parole revocation hearing for a total of three and one-half months and that such delay was not unreasonable. Further, there was no denial of liberty in changing a conditional release date because parole itself was a privilege.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus.
